<p><b>Skopje</b><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[Note 1]</a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/Macedonian_language" title="Macedonian language">Macedonian</a>: <span lang="mk">Скопје</span>, <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Bulgarian_and_Macedonian" title="Help:IPA/Bulgarian and Macedonian">[ˈskɔpjɛ]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Mk-Skopje.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/20/Mk-Skopje.ogg" class="internal" title="Mk-Skopje.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small>) is the capital and <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Macedonia_by_population" class="mw-redirect" title="List of cities in Macedonia by population">largest city</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Republic of Macedonia</a>. It is the country's political, cultural, economic, and academic center. It was known in the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Roman</a> period under the name <i><a href="/wiki/Scupi" title="Scupi">Scupi</a></i>.</p>
<p>The territory of Skopje has been inhabited since at least 4000 BC; remains of <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> settlements have been found within the old <a href="/wiki/Skopje_Fortress" title="Skopje Fortress">Kale Fortress</a> that overlooks the modern city centre. On the eve of the 1st century AD, the settlement was seized by the Romans and became a military camp.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[4]</a></sup> When the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> was divided into eastern and western halves in 395 AD, Scupi came under <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine</a> rule from <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a>. During much of the <a href="/wiki/Early_Middle_Ages" title="Early Middle Ages">early medieval</a> period, the town was contested between the Byzantines and the <a href="/wiki/First_Bulgarian_Empire" title="First Bulgarian Empire">Bulgarian Empire</a>, whose capital it was between 972 and 992. From 1282, the town was part of the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Empire" title="Serbian Empire">Serbian Empire</a> and acted as its capital city from 1346 to 1371. In 1392, the city was conquered by the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Turks</a> who called the town <i>Üsküp</i>. The town stayed under Turkish control for over 500 years, serving as the capital of pashasanjak of Üsküb and later the <a href="/wiki/Vilayet_of_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Vilayet of Kosovo">Vilayet of Kosovo</a>. At that time the city was famous for its oriental architecture<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. In 1912, it was annexed by the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia" title="Kingdom of Serbia">Kingdom of Serbia</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Wars" title="Balkan Wars">Balkan Wars</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERamet2006.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DFTw3lEqi2-oC.26pg.3DPA40.26dq.3Dserbia.2B.2Bannexed.2B.2B1912.26hl.3Dbg.26sa.3DX.26ei.3DoDX8UJnLDovE4gSwnIHgDg.26ved.3D0CDAQ6AEwATgK.23v.3Donepage.26q.3Dserbia.2520.2520annexed.2520.25201912.26f.3Dfalse_40.5D_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERamet2006.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DFTw3lEqi2-oC.26pg.3DPA40.26dq.3Dserbia.2B.2Bannexed.2B.2B1912.26hl.3Dbg.26sa.3DX.26ei.3DoDX8UJnLDovE4gSwnIHgDg.26ved.3D0CDAQ6AEwATgK.23v.3Donepage.26q.3Dserbia.2520.2520annexed.2520.25201912.26f.3Dfalse_40.5D-6">[5]</a></sup> and after the First World War the city became part of the newly formed <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia" title="Kingdom of Yugoslavia">Kingdom of Serbs, Croats and Slovenes (Kingdom of Yugoslavia)</a>. In the Second World War the city was conquered by the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Army#World_War_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Bulgarian Army">Bulgarian Army</a>, which was part of the <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">Axis powers</a>. In 1944, it became the capital city of <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Socialist Republic of Macedonia">Democratic Macedonia</a> (later <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Socialist Republic of Macedonia">Socialist Republic of Macedonia</a>), which was a federal state, part of <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Federal_Yugoslavia" class="mw-redirect" title="Democratic Federal Yugoslavia">Democratic Federal Yugoslavia</a> (later <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia</a>). The city developed rapidly after World War II, but this trend was interrupted in 1963 when it was hit by a <a href="/wiki/1963_Skopje_earthquake" title="1963 Skopje earthquake">disastrous earthquake</a>. In 1991, it became the capital city of an independent Macedonia.</p>
<p>Skopje is located on the upper course of the <a href="/wiki/Vardar" title="Vardar">Vardar River</a>, and is located on a major north-south <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkan</a> route between <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a> and <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a>. It is a center for metal-processing, chemical, timber, textile, leather, and printing industries. Industrial development of the city has been accompanied by development of the trade, logistics, and banking sectors, as well as an emphasis on the fields of transportation, culture and sport. According to the last official count from 2002, Skopje has a population of 506,926 inhabitants; according to more recent unofficial estimates, the city has a population of 502,700 inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Topography">Topography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Topography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Skopje is located in the north of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Republic of Macedonia</a>, in the center of the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Balkan peninsula">Balkan peninsula</a>, and halfway between <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a> and <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a>. The city is built in the Skopje valley, oriented on a west-east axis, along the course of the <a href="/wiki/Vardar" title="Vardar">Vardar</a> river, which flows into the <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean Sea</a> in <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>. The valley is approximately 20 kilometres (12 miles) wide<sup id="cite_ref-tourism_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tourism-8">[7]</a></sup> and it is limited by several mountain ranges to the North and South. These ranges limit the urban expansion of Skopje, which spreads along the Vardar and the Serava, a small river which comes from the North. In its administrative boundaries, the City of Skopje stretches for more than 33 kilometres (21 miles),<sup id="cite_ref-transports_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-transports-9">[8]</a></sup> but it is only 10 kilometres (6.2 miles) wide.<sup id="cite_ref-figures_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-figures-10">[9]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wildflowers_of_Bardovci12.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Wildflowers_of_Bardovci12.jpg/220px-Wildflowers_of_Bardovci12.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Wildflowers_of_Bardovci12.jpg/330px-Wildflowers_of_Bardovci12.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Wildflowers_of_Bardovci12.jpg/440px-Wildflowers_of_Bardovci12.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wildflowers_of_Bardovci12.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Landscape of the Skopje valley, near Bardovci.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Skopje is approximately 245m above sea level and covers 571.46&#160;km<sup>2</sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-drisla_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drisla-11">[10]</a></sup> The urbanised area only covers 337&#160;km<sup>2</sup>, with a density of 65 inhabitants per hectare.<sup id="cite_ref-nature_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nature-12">[11]</a></sup> Skopje, in its administrative limits, encompasses many villages and other settlements, including <a href="/wiki/Dra%C4%8Devo,_Skopje" title="Dračevo, Skopje">Dračevo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gorno_Nerezi" title="Gorno Nerezi">Gorno Nerezi</a> and Bardovci. According to the 2002 census, the City of Skopje comprised 506,926 inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-stats1_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats1-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>The City of Skopje reaches the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a> border to the North-East. Clockwise, it is also bordered by the Macedonian municipalities of <a href="/wiki/%C4%8Cu%C4%8Der-Sandevo_Municipality" title="Čučer-Sandevo Municipality">Čučer-Sandevo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lipkovo_Municipality" title="Lipkovo Municipality">Lipkovo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ara%C4%8Dinovo_Municipality" title="Aračinovo Municipality">Aračinovo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ilinden_Municipality" title="Ilinden Municipality">Ilinden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Studeni%C4%8Dani_Municipality" title="Studeničani Municipality">Studeničani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sopi%C5%A1te_Municipality" title="Sopište Municipality">Sopište</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDelino_Municipality" title="Želino Municipality">Želino</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jegunovce_Municipality" title="Jegunovce Municipality">Jegunovce</a>.</p>
<div class="center">
<div class="thumb tnone">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:442px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_City_of_Skopje_en.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Map_City_of_Skopje_en.svg/440px-Map_City_of_Skopje_en.svg.png" width="440" height="258" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Map_City_of_Skopje_en.svg/660px-Map_City_of_Skopje_en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Map_City_of_Skopje_en.svg/880px-Map_City_of_Skopje_en.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1550" data-file-height="910" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_City_of_Skopje_en.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The City of Skopje, its administrative limits are in red.</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hydrography">Hydrography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Hydrography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Skopje_X31.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Skopje_X31.jpg/220px-Skopje_X31.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Skopje_X31.jpg/330px-Skopje_X31.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Skopje_X31.jpg/440px-Skopje_X31.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Skopje_X31.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Vardar" title="Vardar">Vardar</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Stone_Bridge_(Skopje)" title="Stone Bridge (Skopje)">Stone Bridge</a>, symbol of the city.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Vardar" title="Vardar">Vardar</a> river, which flows through Skopje, is at approximately 60 kilometres (37 miles) from its source near <a href="/wiki/Gostivar" title="Gostivar">Gostivar</a>. In Skopje, its average discharge is 51 m<sup>3</sup>/s, with a wide amplitude depending on seasons, between 99.6 m<sup>3</sup>/s in May and 18.7 m<sup>3</sup>/s in July. The water temperature is comprised between 4.6&#160;°C in January and 18.1&#160;°C in July.<sup id="cite_ref-vardar_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vardar-13">[12]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Del_od_Skopje,_1950ti.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Del_od_Skopje%2C_1950ti.jpg/220px-Del_od_Skopje%2C_1950ti.jpg" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Del_od_Skopje%2C_1950ti.jpg/330px-Del_od_Skopje%2C_1950ti.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Del_od_Skopje%2C_1950ti.jpg/440px-Del_od_Skopje%2C_1950ti.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2196" data-file-height="1620" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Del_od_Skopje,_1950ti.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The main river running through the center of Skopje c. 1950</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Several rivers meet the Vardar within the city boundaries. The largest is the <a href="/wiki/Treska" title="Treska">Treska</a>, which is 130 kilometres (81 miles) long. It crosses the <a href="/wiki/Matka_Canyon" title="Matka Canyon">Matka Canyon</a> before reaching the Vardar on the western extremity of the City of Skopje. The <a href="/wiki/Lepenac" title="Lepenac">Lepenec</a>, coming from <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>, flows into the Vardar on the northwestern end of the urban area. The Serava, also coming from the North, had flowed through the <a href="/wiki/Old_Bazaar,_Skopje" title="Old Bazaar, Skopje">Old Bazaar</a> until the 1960s, when it was diverted towards the West because its waters were very polluted. Originally, it met the Vardar close to the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_Academy_of_Sciences_and_Arts" title="Macedonian Academy of Sciences and Arts">Macedonian Academy of Sciences and Arts</a>. Nowadays, it flows into the Vardar near the ruins of <a href="/wiki/Scupi" title="Scupi">Scupi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup> Finally, the Markova Reka, the source of which is on Mount <a href="/wiki/Vodno" title="Vodno">Vodno</a>, meets the Vardar at the eastern extremity of the city. These three rivers are less than 70 kilometres (43 miles) long.<sup id="cite_ref-figures_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-figures-10">[9]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9A%D0%B0%D1%9A%D0%BE%D0%BD.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/%D0%9A%D0%B0%D1%9A%D0%BE%D0%BD.jpg/220px-%D0%9A%D0%B0%D1%9A%D0%BE%D0%BD.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/%D0%9A%D0%B0%D1%9A%D0%BE%D0%BD.jpg/330px-%D0%9A%D0%B0%D1%9A%D0%BE%D0%BD.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/%D0%9A%D0%B0%D1%9A%D0%BE%D0%BD.jpg/440px-%D0%9A%D0%B0%D1%9A%D0%BE%D0%BD.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9A%D0%B0%D1%9A%D0%BE%D0%BD.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Matka_Canyon" title="Matka Canyon">Matka Canyon</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Treska" title="Treska">Treska</a>, on the western edge of the City of Skopje.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city of Skopje comprises two artificial lakes, located on the Treska. The lake Matka is the result of the construction of a dam in the Matka Canyon in the 1930s, and the Treska lake was dug for leisure purpose in 1978.<sup id="cite_ref-figures_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-figures-10">[9]</a></sup> Three small natural lakes can be found near Smiljkovci, on the northeastern edge of the urban area.</p>
<p>The river <a href="/wiki/Vardar" title="Vardar">Vardar</a> historically caused many floods, such as in 1962, when its outflow reached 1110 m<sup>3</sup>/s<sup>−1</sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-vardar_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vardar-13">[12]</a></sup> Several works have been carried since Byzantine times to limit the risks, and since the construction of the Kozjak dam on the Treska in 1994, the flood risk is close to zero.<sup id="cite_ref-kozjak_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kozjak-15">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>The subsoil contains a large <a href="/wiki/Water_table" title="Water table">water table</a> which is alimented by the Vardar river and functions as an underground river. Under the table lies an <a href="/wiki/Aquifer" title="Aquifer">aquifer</a> contained in <a href="/wiki/Marl" title="Marl">marl</a>. The water table is 4 to 12 m under the ground and 4 to 144 m deep. Several wells collect its waters but most of the drinking water used in Skopje comes from a <a href="/wiki/Karst" title="Karst">karstic</a> spring in Rašče, located west of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-nature_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nature-12">[11]</a></sup></p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162px">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Skopje_X90.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Skopje_X90.JPG/220px-Skopje_X90.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Skopje_X90.JPG/330px-Skopje_X90.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Skopje_X90.JPG/440px-Skopje_X90.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Skopje_X90.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mount <a href="/wiki/Vodno" title="Vodno">Vodno</a> as seen from the <a href="/wiki/Stone_Bridge_(Skopje)" title="Stone Bridge (Skopje)">Stone Bridge</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Skopje valley is bordered on the West by the <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0ar_Mountains" title="Šar Mountains">Šar Mountains</a>, on the South by the <a href="/wiki/Jakupica" title="Jakupica">Jakupica</a> range, on the East by hills belonging to the <a href="/wiki/Osogovo" title="Osogovo">Osogovo</a> range, and on the North by the <a href="/wiki/Skopska_Crna_Gora" title="Skopska Crna Gora">Skopska Crna Gora</a>. Mount <a href="/wiki/Vodno" title="Vodno">Vodno</a>, the highest point inside the city limits, is 1066 m high and is part of the <a href="/wiki/Jakupica" title="Jakupica">Jakupica</a> range.<sup id="cite_ref-figures_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-figures-10">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although Skopje is built on the foot of Mount Vodno, the urban area is mostly flat. It comprises several minor hills, generally covered with woods and parks, such as Gazi Baba hill (325 m), Zajčev Rid (327 m), the foothills of Mount Vodno (the smallest are between 350 and 400 m high) and the promontory on which <a href="/wiki/Skopje_Fortress" title="Skopje Fortress">Skopje Fortress</a> is built.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cave_lake_(8172274819).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Cave_lake_%288172274819%29.jpg/220px-Cave_lake_%288172274819%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Cave_lake_%288172274819%29.jpg/330px-Cave_lake_%288172274819%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Cave_lake_%288172274819%29.jpg/440px-Cave_lake_%288172274819%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3537" data-file-height="2358" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cave_lake_(8172274819).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A cave near the <a href="/wiki/Matka_Canyon" title="Matka Canyon">Matka Canyon</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Skopje valley is located near a seismic fault between the African and Eurasian <a href="/wiki/Tectonic_plate" class="mw-redirect" title="Tectonic plate">tectonic plates</a> and experiences regular seismic activity.<sup id="cite_ref-damages_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-damages-17">[16]</a></sup> This activity in enhanced by the porous structure of the subsoil.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[17]</a></sup> Large earthquakes occurred in Skopje in 518, 1505 and 1963.<sup id="cite_ref-damages_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-damages-17">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Skopje valley belongs to the Vardar geotectonic region, the subsoil of which is formed of <a href="/wiki/Neogene" title="Neogene">Neogene</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quaternary" title="Quaternary">Quaternary</a> deposits. The substratum is made of <a href="/wiki/Pliocene" title="Pliocene">Pliocene</a> deposits including <a href="/wiki/Sandstone" title="Sandstone">sandstone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marl" title="Marl">marl</a> and various conglomerates. It is covered by a first layer of Quaternary sands and silt, which is between 70 and 90 m deep. The layer is topped by a much smaller layer of clay, sand, silt and gravel, carried by the <a href="/wiki/Vardar" title="Vardar">Vardar</a> river. It is between 1.5 and 5.2 m deep.<sup id="cite_ref-ohis_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohis-19">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>In some areas, the subsoil is <a href="/wiki/Karst" title="Karst">karstic</a>. It led to the formation of canyons, such as the <a href="/wiki/Matka_Canyon" title="Matka Canyon">Matka Canyon</a>, which is surrounded by ten caves. They are between 20 and 176 m deep.<sup id="cite_ref-macedonia.co.uk_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-macedonia.co.uk-20">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The climate of Skopje is usually classified as continental sub-Mediterranean,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate"><i>Cfa</i></a> under the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>) with a mean annual temperature of 13.5&#160;°C (56&#160;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup> Precipitation is relatively low due to the pronounced <a href="/wiki/Rain_shadow" title="Rain shadow">rain shadow</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Prokletije" title="Prokletije">Prokletije</a> mountains to the northwest, being only a quarter of what is received on the Adriatic Sea coast at the same latitude. The summers are long, hot and humid. Skopje's average July high is 31&#160;°C (88&#160;°F). On average Skopje will see 88 days above 30&#160;°C (86&#160;°F) each year, and 10.2 days above 35.0&#160;°C (95&#160;°F) every year. Winters are short, relatively cold, and wet. Snowfalls are common in the winter period, but heavy snow accumulation is rare and the snowcover lasts only for a few hours or a few days if heavy. In summer, temperatures are usually above 31&#160;°C (88&#160;°F) and sometimes above 40&#160;°C (104&#160;°F). In spring and autumn, the temperatures range from 15 to 24&#160;°C (59 to 75&#160;°F). In winter, the day temperatures are roughly 6&#160;°C (43&#160;°F), but at nights they often fall below 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F) and sometimes below −10&#160;°C (14&#160;°F). Typically, temperatures throughout one year range from −13&#160;°C to 39&#160;°C. Occurrences of precipitation are evenly distributed throughout the year, being heaviest from October to December and from April to June.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nature_and_environment">Nature and environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Nature and environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mt._Vodno1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Mt._Vodno1.jpg/220px-Mt._Vodno1.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Mt._Vodno1.jpg/330px-Mt._Vodno1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Mt._Vodno1.jpg/440px-Mt._Vodno1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mt._Vodno1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Skopje as seen from Mount Vodno. The cable car cables are also visible.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city of Skopje encompasses various natural environments and its fauna and flora are rich. However, it is threatened by the intensification of agriculture and the urban extension. The largest protected area within the city limits is Mount Vodno, which is a popular leisure destination. A cable car connects its peak to the downtown, and many pedestrian paths run through its woods. Other large natural spots include the <a href="/wiki/Matka_Canyon" title="Matka Canyon">Matka Canyon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nature_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nature-12">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city itself comprises several parks and gardens amounting to 4,361 hectares. Among these are the City Park (Gradski Park), built by the Ottoman Turks at the beginning of the 20th century; Žena Borec Park, located in front of the Parliament; the University arboretum; and Gazi Baba forest. Many streets and boulevards are planted with trees.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>Skopje experiences many environmental issues which are often overshadowed by the economic poverty of the country. However, alignment of Macedonian law on European law has brought progress in some fields, such as water and waste treatment, and industrial emissions.<sup id="cite_ref-pol_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pol-28">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>Steel processing, which a crucial activity for the local economy, is responsible for soil pollution with heavy metals such as <a href="/wiki/Lead" title="Lead">lead</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">zinc</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cadmium" title="Cadmium">cadmium</a>, and air pollution with <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_oxide" title="Nitrogen oxide">nitrogen oxide</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carbon_monoxide" title="Carbon monoxide">carbon monoxide</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nature_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nature-12">[11]</a></sup> Vehicle traffic and <a href="/wiki/District_heating" title="District heating">district heating</a> plants are also responsible for air pollution. The highest pollution levels usually occur in autumn and winter.<sup id="cite_ref-pol_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pol-28">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>Water treatment plants are being built, but much polluted water is still discharged untreated into the <a href="/wiki/Vardar" title="Vardar">Vardar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nature_12-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nature-12">[11]</a></sup> Waste is disposed of in the open-air municipal landfill site, located 15 kilometres (9.3 miles) north of the city. Every day, it receives 1,500 m<sup>3</sup> of domestic waste and 400 m<sup>3</sup> of industrial waste. Health levels are better in Skopje than in the rest of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Republic of Macedonia</a>, and no link has been found between the low environmental quality and the health of the residents.<sup id="cite_ref-security_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-security-29">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Urbanism">Urbanism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Urbanism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_morphology">Urban morphology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Urban morphology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:GUP_Skopje_2002_mal.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/GUP_Skopje_2002_mal.jpg/220px-GUP_Skopje_2002_mal.jpg" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/GUP_Skopje_2002_mal.jpg/330px-GUP_Skopje_2002_mal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/GUP_Skopje_2002_mal.jpg/440px-GUP_Skopje_2002_mal.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="618" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:GUP_Skopje_2002_mal.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Skopje urban plan for 2002–2020&#160;:
<div>
<div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #A42424; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;City centre</div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FFA500; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Collective housing</div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FFF48D; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Individual housing</div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #5472AE; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Industrial areas</div>
</div>
<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:100%;">
<tr>
<td></td>
</tr>
</table>
</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The urban morphology of Skopje was deeply impacted by the 26th of July <a href="/wiki/1963_Skopje_earthquake" title="1963 Skopje earthquake">1963 earthquake</a> which destroyed 80% of the city and by the reconstruction that followed.<sup id="cite_ref-damages_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-damages-17">[16]</a></sup> For instance, neighbourhoods were rebuilt in such a way that the demographic density remains low to limit the impact of potential future earthquakes.<sup id="cite_ref-post_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-post-30">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>Reconstruction following the 1963 earthquake was mainly conducted by the Polish architect <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Ciborowski" title="Adolf Ciborowski">Adolf Ciborowski</a>, who had already planned the reconstruction of <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a> after <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. Ciborowski divided the city in blocks dedicated to specific activities. The banks of the <a href="/wiki/Vardar" title="Vardar">Vardar</a> river became natural areas and parks, areas located between the main boulevards were built with highrise housing and shopping malls, and the suburbs were left to individual housing and industry.<sup id="cite_ref-reconstruction_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reconstruction-31">[30]</a></sup> Reconstruction had to be quick in order to relocate families and to relaunch the local economy. To stimulate economic development, the number of thoroughfares was increased and future urban extension was anticipated.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Skopje_SPOT_1114.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Skopje_SPOT_1114.jpg/220px-Skopje_SPOT_1114.jpg" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Skopje_SPOT_1114.jpg/330px-Skopje_SPOT_1114.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Skopje_SPOT_1114.jpg/440px-Skopje_SPOT_1114.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="500" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Skopje_SPOT_1114.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Skopje as seen by the <a href="/wiki/SPOT_(satellite)" title="SPOT (satellite)">SPOT satellite</a>. Mount Vodno is visible on the bottom left of the picture.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The south bank of the Vardar river generally comprises highrise tower blocks, including the vast Karpoš neighbourhood which was built in the 1970s west of the centre. Towards the East, the new municipality of <a href="/wiki/Aerodrom_Municipality_(Skopje)" class="mw-redirect" title="Aerodrom Municipality (Skopje)">Aerodrom</a> was planned in the 1980s to house 80,000 inhabitants on the site of the old airport. Between Karpoš and Aerodrom lies the city centre, rebuilt according to plans by Japanese architect <a href="/wiki/Kenzo_Tange" class="mw-redirect" title="Kenzo Tange">Kenzo Tange</a>. The centre is surrounded by a row of long buildings suggesting a wall ("Gradski Zid").<sup id="cite_ref-post_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-post-30">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>On the north bank, where the most ancient parts of the city lie, the <a href="/wiki/Old_Bazaar,_Skopje" title="Old Bazaar, Skopje">Old Bazaar</a> was restored and its surroundings were rebuilt with low-rise buildings, so as not to spoil views of the <a href="/wiki/Skopje_Fortress" title="Skopje Fortress">Skopje Fortress</a>. Several institutions, including the university and the Macedonian academy, were also relocated on the north bank in order to reduce borders between the ethnic communities. Indeed, the north bank is mostly inhabited by Muslim Albanians, Turks and Roma, whereas Christian ethnic Macedonians predominantly reside on the south bank.<sup id="cite_ref-reconstruction_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reconstruction-31">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>The earthquake left the city with few historical monuments, apart from the Ottoman <a href="/wiki/Old_Bazaar,_Skopje" title="Old Bazaar, Skopje">Old Bazaar</a>, and the reconstruction, conducted between the 1960s and 1980s, turned Skopje into a <a href="/wiki/Modernist_architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Modernist architecture">modernist</a> but grey city. At the end of the <a href="/wiki/2000s_(decade)" title="2000s (decade)">2000s</a>, the city center experienced profound changes. A highly controversial<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup> urban project, "<a href="/wiki/Skopje_2014" title="Skopje 2014">Skopje 2014</a>", was adopted by the municipal authorities in order to give the city a more monumental and historical aspect, and thus to transform it into a proper national capital. Several neoclassical buildings destroyed in the 1963 earthquake were rebuilt, including the national theatre, and streets and squares were refurbished. Many other elements were also built, including fountains, statues, hotels, government buildings and bridges. The project has been criticised because of its cost and its historicist aesthetics.<sup id="cite_ref-objections_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-objections-34">[33]</a></sup> The large Albanian minority felt it was not represented in the new monuments,<sup id="cite_ref-Albanian_objections_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Albanian_objections-35">[34]</a></sup> and launched side projects, including a new square over the boulevard that separate the city centre from the <a href="/wiki/Old_Bazaar,_Skopje" title="Old Bazaar, Skopje">Old Bazaar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some areas of Skopje suffer from a certain anarchy because many houses and buildings were built without consent from the local authorities.<sup id="cite_ref-eco_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eco-37">[36]</a></sup></p>

</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Localities_and_villages">Localities and villages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Localities and villages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gorno_Nerezi_2013_(1).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Gorno_Nerezi_2013_%281%29.JPG/220px-Gorno_Nerezi_2013_%281%29.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Gorno_Nerezi_2013_%281%29.JPG/330px-Gorno_Nerezi_2013_%281%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Gorno_Nerezi_2013_%281%29.JPG/440px-Gorno_Nerezi_2013_%281%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4272" data-file-height="2848" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gorno_Nerezi_2013_(1).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Gorno_Nerezi" title="Gorno Nerezi">Gorno Nerezi</a>, a village located on the northern side of Mount Vodno.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Outside of the urban area, the City of Skopje encompasses many small settlements. Some of them are becoming outer suburbs, such as Singeliḱ, located on the road to Belgrade, which has more than 23,000 inhabitants, and <a href="/wiki/Dra%C4%8Devo,_Skopje" title="Dračevo, Skopje">Dračevo</a>, which has almost 20,000 inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-dwelling_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dwelling-38">[37]</a></sup> Other large settlements are located north of the city, such as Radišani, with 9,000 inhabitants,<sup id="cite_ref-dwelling_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dwelling-38">[37]</a></sup> whereas smaller villages can be found on Mount Vodno or in <a href="/wiki/Saraj_municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Saraj municipality">Saraj municipality</a>, which is the most rural of the ten municipalities that form the City of Skopje.<sup id="cite_ref-region_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-region-39">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some localities located outside the city limits are also becoming outer suburbs, particularly in <a href="/wiki/Ilinden_municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Ilinden municipality">Ilinden</a> and <a href="/wiki/Petrovec_municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Petrovec municipality">Petrovec municipality</a>. They benefit from the presence of major roads, railways and the <a href="/wiki/Skopje_%22Alexander_the_Great%22_Airport" title="Skopje &quot;Alexander the Great&quot; Airport">airport</a>, located in Petrovec.<sup id="cite_ref-region_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-region-39">[38]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_sociology">Urban sociology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Urban sociology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kapistec.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Kapistec.jpg/220px-Kapistec.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Kapistec.jpg/330px-Kapistec.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Kapistec.jpg/440px-Kapistec.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kapistec.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Kapištec neighbourhood, developed during the 1970s. Some post-earthquake prefabricated houses can be seen in the foreground.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Skopje is an ethnically diverse city, and its urban sociology primarily depends on ethnic and religious belonging. <a href="/wiki/Macedonians_(ethnic_group)" title="Macedonians (ethnic group)">Macedonians</a> form 66% of the city population, while <a href="/wiki/Albanians_in_the_Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Albanians in the Republic of Macedonia">Albanians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roma_in_the_Republic_of_Macedonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Roma in the Republic of Macedonia">Roma</a> account respectively for 20% and 6%.<sup id="cite_ref-stats1_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats1-1">[1]</a></sup> Each ethnic group generally restrict itself to certain areas of the city. Macedonians live south of the <a href="/wiki/Vardar" title="Vardar">Vardar</a>, in areas massively rebuilt after 1963, and Muslims live on the northern side, in the oldest neighbourhoods of the city. These neighbourhoods are considered more traditional, whereas the south side evokes to Macedonians modernity and rupture from rural life.<sup id="cite_ref-thiesen57_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thiesen57-40">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>The northern areas are the poorest. This is especially true for <a href="/wiki/Topaana" title="Topaana">Topaana</a>, in <a href="/wiki/%C4%8Cair_municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Čair municipality">Čair municipality</a>, and for <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0uto_Orizari_municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Šuto Orizari municipality">Šuto Orizari municipality</a>, which are the two main Roma neighbourhoods. They are made of many illegal constructions not connected to electricity and water supply, which are passed from a generation to the other. Topaana, located close to the <a href="/wiki/Old_Bazaar,_Skopje" title="Old Bazaar, Skopje">Old Bazaar</a>, is a very old area: it was first mentioned as a Roma neighbourhood in the beginning of the 14th century. It has between 3,000 and 5,000 inhabitants. Šuto Orizari, located on the northern edge of the city, is a municipality of its own, with <a href="/wiki/Romani_language" title="Romani language">Romani</a> as its local official language. It was developed after the <a href="/wiki/1963_Skopje_earthquake" title="1963 Skopje earthquake">1963 earthquake</a> to accommodate Roma who had lost their house.<sup id="cite_ref-roma_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roma-41">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">population density</a> varies greatly from an area to the other. So does the size of the living area per person. The city average was at 19.41 square metres (208.93 square feet) per person as of 2002<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, but at 24 square metres (258 square feet) in <a href="/wiki/Centar_municipality_(Skopje)" class="mw-redirect" title="Centar municipality (Skopje)">Centar</a> on the south bank, and only 14 square metres (151 square feet) in <a href="/wiki/%C4%8Cair_municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Čair municipality">Čair</a> on the north bank. In <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0uto_Orizari_municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Šuto Orizari municipality">Šuto Orizari</a>, the average was at 13 square metres (140 square feet).<sup id="cite_ref-stats1_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats1-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Toponymy">Toponymy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Toponymy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Names_of_European_cities_in_different_languages:_Q-T#S" class="mw-redirect" title="Names of European cities in different languages: Q-T">other names of Skopje</a></div>
<p>The current name of the city comes from "Scupi", which was the name of a <a href="/wiki/Roman_colony" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman colony">Roman colony</a> located nearby. However, before the colony was created, the site had already been settled by <a href="/wiki/Illyrians" title="Illyrians">Illyrians</a> and "Scupi" is probably of Illyrian origin.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The meaning of that name is unknown.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>After <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">Antiquity</a>, Scupi was occupied by various people and consequently its name was translated several times in several languages. Thus Scupi became "Skopie" (<a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_language" title="Bulgarian language">Bulgarian</a>: <span lang="bg">Скопие</span>) for Bulgarians,<sup id="cite_ref-history_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-43">[42]</a></sup> and later "Üsküb" (<a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turkish_language" title="Ottoman Turkish language">Ottoman Turkish</a>: <span lang="ota-Arab" dir="rtl">اسكوب</span>‎) for the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Turks</a>. This name was adapted in Western languages in "Uskub" or "Uskup", and these two appellations were used in the Western world until 1912. Some Western sources also cite "Scopia" and "Skopia".<sup id="cite_ref-britannica_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-44">[43]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Skoplje_1912.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Skoplje_1912.jpg/220px-Skoplje_1912.jpg" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Skoplje_1912.jpg/330px-Skoplje_1912.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Skoplje_1912.jpg/440px-Skoplje_1912.jpg 2x" data-file-width="583" data-file-height="377" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Skoplje_1912.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Serbian troops overseeing the city's renaming from "Üsküb" to "Skoplje" following Serbia's annexation of Macedonia in 1912</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>When <a href="/wiki/Vardar_Macedonia" title="Vardar Macedonia">Vardar Macedonia</a> was annexed by the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia" title="Kingdom of Serbia">Kingdom of Serbia</a> in 1912, the city officially became "Skoplje" and this name was adopted by many languages. The city eventually became "Skopje" (<a href="/wiki/Macedonian_language" title="Macedonian language">Macedonian</a>: <span lang="mk">Скопје</span>) after the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>, when standard <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_language" title="Macedonian language">Macedonian</a> became the official language of the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Socialist Republic of Macedonia">Socialist Republic of Macedonia</a>. The Albanian minority calls the city "Shkup" and "Shkupi", the latter being the definite form, and Roma call it "Skopiye".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHeroldLangerLechler201029_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeroldLangerLechler201029-45">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Skopje" title="History of Skopje">History of Skopje</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Skopje" title="Timeline of Skopje">Timeline of Skopje</a></div>
