</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The rocky promontory on which stands the <a href="/wiki/Skopje_Fortress" title="Skopje Fortress">Fortress</a> was the first site settled by man in Skopje. The earliest vestiges of human occupation found on this site date from the <a href="/wiki/Chalcolithic" title="Chalcolithic">Chalcolithic</a> (<a href="/wiki/4th_millennium_BC" title="4th millennium BC">4th millennium BC</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-kalepre_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kalepre-48">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although the Chalcolithic settlement must have been of some significance, it declined during the <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a>. Archeological research suggest that the settlement always belonged to a same culture, which progressively evolved thanks to contacts with <a href="/wiki/Balkan" class="mw-redirect" title="Balkan">Balkan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> cultures, and later with the <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean</a>. The locality eventually disappeared during the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a><sup id="cite_ref-kaleant_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kaleant-49">[46]</a></sup> when <a href="/wiki/Scupi" title="Scupi">Scupi</a> emerged. Scupi was originally an <a href="/wiki/Illyrians" title="Illyrians">Illyrian</a> settlement founded during the 1st millennium BC but it later became a <a href="/wiki/Dardani" title="Dardani">Dardanian</a> town.<sup id="cite_ref-history_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-43">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[47]</a></sup> It was located on Zajčev Rid hill, some 5 kilometres (3.1&#160;mi) west of the fortress promontory. Located at the centre of the Balkan peninsula and on the road between <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean Sea</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-provincial_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-provincial-51">[48]</a></sup> it was a prosperous locality, although its history is not well known.<sup id="cite_ref-provincial_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-provincial-51">[48]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roman_Scupi">Roman Scupi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Roman Scupi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Shy_venus_statue_skopje.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Shy_venus_statue_skopje.jpg/220px-Shy_venus_statue_skopje.jpg" width="220" height="418" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Shy_venus_statue_skopje.jpg/330px-Shy_venus_statue_skopje.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/37/Shy_venus_statue_skopje.jpg 2x" data-file-width="343" data-file-height="651" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Shy_venus_statue_skopje.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A "Venus Pudica" found in Scupi, dated from the 2nd century AD.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Dardani" title="Dardani">Dardanians</a>, who lived in present-day <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>, invaded the region around Skopje during the 3rd century BC. <i><a href="/wiki/Scupi" title="Scupi">Scupi</a></i>, the ancient name for Skopje, became the capital of Dardania, which extended from <a href="/wiki/Naissus" class="mw-redirect" title="Naissus">Naissus</a> to <a href="/wiki/Bylazora" title="Bylazora">Bylazora</a> in the second century BC.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[49]</a></sup> The Dardanians had remained independent after the Roman conquest of <a href="/wiki/Macedon" class="mw-redirect" title="Macedon">Macedon</a>, and it seems most likely that Dardania lost independence in 28 BC.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[50]</a></sup> Roman expansion east brought Scupi under Roman rule as a colony of legionnaires, mainly veterans of the Legio IIV Claudia in the time of <a href="/wiki/Domitian" title="Domitian">Domitian</a> (81–96 AD). However, several legions from the <a href="/wiki/Roman_province_of_Macedonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman province of Macedonia">Roman province of Macedonia</a> of <a href="/wiki/Crassus" class="mw-redirect" title="Crassus">Crassus</a>' army may already have been stationed in there around 29–28 BC, before the official imperial command was instituted.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[52]</a></sup> The first mention of the city was made at that period by <a href="/wiki/Livy" title="Livy">Livy</a>, who died in 17 AD.<sup id="cite_ref-history_43-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-43">[42]</a></sup> Scupi first served as a military base to maintain peace in the region<sup id="cite_ref-provincial_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-provincial-51">[48]</a></sup> and was officially named "Colonia Flavia Scupinorum", <i>Flavia</i> being the name of the <a href="/wiki/Flavian_dynasty" title="Flavian dynasty">emperor's dynasty</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-archeology_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-archeology-56">[53]</a></sup> Shortly afterwards it became part of the province of <a href="/wiki/Moesia" title="Moesia">Moesia</a> during <a href="/wiki/Augustus" title="Augustus">Augustus</a>'s rule.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[54]</a></sup> After the division of the province by <a href="/wiki/Domitian" title="Domitian">Domitian</a> in 86 AD, Scupi was elevated to colonial status, and became a seat of government within the new province of <a href="/wiki/Moesia_Superior" class="mw-redirect" title="Moesia Superior">Moesia Superior</a>. The district called <a href="/wiki/Dardania_(Europe)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dardania (Europe)">Dardania</a> (within Moesia Superior) was formed into a special province by Diocletian, with the capital at <a href="/wiki/Naissus" class="mw-redirect" title="Naissus">Naissus</a>.</p>
<p>The city population was very diverse. Engravings on tombstones suggest that only a minority of the population came from <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, while many veterans were from <a href="/wiki/Dalmatia" title="Dalmatia">Dalmatia</a>, South <a href="/wiki/Gaul" title="Gaul">Gaul</a> and <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>. Because of the ethnic diversity of the population, <a href="/wiki/Latin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin language">Latin</a> maintained itself as the main language in the city at the expense of <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">Greek</a>, which was spoken in most of the Moesian and Macedonian cities.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[55]</a></sup> During the following centuries, Scupi experienced prosperity. The period from the end of the 3rd century to the end of the 4th century was particularly flourishing.<sup id="cite_ref-archeology_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-archeology-56">[53]</a></sup> A first church was founded under the reign of <a href="/wiki/Constantine_the_Great" title="Constantine the Great">Constantine the Great</a> and Scupi became the seat of a diocese. In 395, following the division of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> in two, Scupi became part of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Roman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Roman Empire">Eastern Roman Empire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-history_43-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-43">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>In its heyday, Scupi covered 40 hectares and was closed by a 3.5-metre (11&#160;ft) wide wall.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[56]</a></sup> It had many monuments, including four necropoles, a theatre, thermae,<sup id="cite_ref-archeology_56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-archeology-56">[53]</a></sup> and a large Christian basilica.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[57]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tvrdina_vo_Skopje-Makedonija_79_(5).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Tvrdina_vo_Skopje-Makedonija_79_%285%29.JPG/220px-Tvrdina_vo_Skopje-Makedonija_79_%285%29.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Tvrdina_vo_Skopje-Makedonija_79_%285%29.JPG/330px-Tvrdina_vo_Skopje-Makedonija_79_%285%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Tvrdina_vo_Skopje-Makedonija_79_%285%29.JPG/440px-Tvrdina_vo_Skopje-Makedonija_79_%285%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tvrdina_vo_Skopje-Makedonija_79_(5).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Skopje_Fortress" title="Skopje Fortress">Skopje Fortress</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 518, Scupi was destroyed by a violent earthquake,<sup id="cite_ref-damages_17-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-damages-17">[16]</a></sup> possibly the most devastating one Macedonia has ever experienced.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[58]</a></sup> At that time, the region was threatened by the <a href="/wiki/Barbarian_invasions" class="mw-redirect" title="Barbarian invasions">Barbarian invasions</a>, and the city inhabitants had already fled in forests and mountains before the disaster occurred.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[59]</a></sup> Scupi was eventually rebuilt by <a href="/wiki/Justinian_I" title="Justinian I">Justinian I</a>. During his reign, many Byzantine towns were relocated on hills and other easily defendable places to face invasions. Scupi was thus transferred on another site: the promontory on which stands the <a href="/wiki/Skopje_Fortress" title="Skopje Fortress">fortress</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[60]</a></sup> However, Scupi was sacked by <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavs</a> at the end of the 6th century and the city seems to have fallen under Slavic rule in 695.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[61]</a></sup> The Slavic tribe which settled in Scupi were probably the Berziti<sup id="cite_ref-history_43-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-43">[42]</a></sup> who had invaded the entire <a href="/wiki/Vardar" title="Vardar">Vardar</a> valley.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[62]</a></sup> The city is not mentioned during the three following centuries<sup id="cite_ref-history_43-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-43">[42]</a></sup> but along with the rest of Upper Vardar it became part of the expanding <a href="/wiki/First_Bulgarian_Empire" title="First Bulgarian Empire">First Bulgarian Empire</a> in the 830s.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[63]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[64]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Coronation_of_Emperor_Du%C5%A1an,_in_%22The_Slavonic_Epic%22_(1926).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Coronation_of_Emperor_Du%C5%A1an%2C_in_%22The_Slavonic_Epic%22_%281926%29.jpg/220px-Coronation_of_Emperor_Du%C5%A1an%2C_in_%22The_Slavonic_Epic%22_%281926%29.jpg" width="220" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Coronation_of_Emperor_Du%C5%A1an%2C_in_%22The_Slavonic_Epic%22_%281926%29.jpg/330px-Coronation_of_Emperor_Du%C5%A1an%2C_in_%22The_Slavonic_Epic%22_%281926%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Coronation_of_Emperor_Du%C5%A1an%2C_in_%22The_Slavonic_Epic%22_%281926%29.jpg/440px-Coronation_of_Emperor_Du%C5%A1an%2C_in_%22The_Slavonic_Epic%22_%281926%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1020" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Coronation_of_Emperor_Du%C5%A1an,_in_%22The_Slavonic_Epic%22_(1926).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The coronation of emperor <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Uro%C5%A1_IV_Du%C5%A1an_of_Serbia" class="mw-redirect" title="Stephen Uroš IV Dušan of Serbia">Dušan</a> in Skopje, <a href="/wiki/Alfons_Mucha" class="mw-redirect" title="Alfons Mucha">Alfons Mucha</a>, 1926.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Starting from the end of the 10th century Skopje experienced a period of wars and political troubles. Bulgarian capital from 972 to 992, <a href="/wiki/Samuel_of_Bulgaria" title="Samuel of Bulgaria">Samuil</a> ruled it from 976<sup id="cite_ref-kalemed_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kalemed-68">[65]</a></sup> until 1004 when its governor Roman surrendered it to Byzantine Emperor <a href="/wiki/Basil_II" title="Basil II">Basil the Bulgar Slayer</a> in 1004 in exchange of the titles of patrician and strategos.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[66]</a></sup> Later, Skopje was briefly seized twice by Slavic insurgents who wanted to restore a Bulgarian state. At first in 1040 under <a href="/wiki/Peter_Delyan" title="Peter Delyan">Peter Delyan</a>'s command,<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[67]</a></sup> and in 1072 under the orders of <a href="/wiki/Georgi_Voyteh" title="Georgi Voyteh">Georgi Voyteh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[68]</a></sup> In 1081, Skopje was captured by <a href="/wiki/Normans" title="Normans">Norman</a> troops led by <a href="/wiki/Robert_Guiscard" title="Robert Guiscard">Robert Guiscard</a> and the city remained in their hands until 1088. Skopje was subsequently conquered by the Serbian Grand Prince <a href="/wiki/Vukan,_Grand_Prince_of_Serbia" title="Vukan, Grand Prince of Serbia">Vukan</a> in 1093, and again by the Normans four years later. However, because of epidemics and food shortage, Normans quickly surrendered to the Byzantines.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the 12th and 13th centuries, Bulgarians and Serbs took advantage of Byzantine decline to create large kingdoms stretching from <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean Sea</a>. <a href="/wiki/Kaloyan_of_Bulgaria" title="Kaloyan of Bulgaria">Kaloyan</a> brought Skopje back into <a href="/wiki/Second_Bulgarian_Empire" title="Second Bulgarian Empire">reestablished Bulgaria</a> in 1203<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[70]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-John_Van_Antwerp_Fine_1994_175.E2.80.93184_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-John_Van_Antwerp_Fine_1994_175.E2.80.93184-74">[71]</a></sup> until his nephew <a href="/wiki/Strez" title="Strez">Strez</a> declared autonomy along the Upper Vardar with Serbian help only five years later.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[72]</a></sup> In 1209 Strez switched allegiances and recognized <a href="/wiki/Boril_of_Bulgaria" title="Boril of Bulgaria">Boril of Bulgaria</a> with whom he led a successful joint campaign against Serbia's first internationally recognized king <a href="/wiki/Stefan_the_First-Crowned" title="Stefan the First-Crowned">Stefan Nemanjić</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-John_Van_Antwerp_Fine_1994_175.E2.80.93184_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-John_Van_Antwerp_Fine_1994_175.E2.80.93184-74">[71]</a></sup> From 1214 to 1230 Skopje was a part of Byzantine successor state <a href="/wiki/Despotate_of_Epirus" title="Despotate of Epirus">Epirus</a> before recaptured by <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Asen_II_of_Bulgaria" title="Ivan Asen II of Bulgaria">Ivan Asen II</a> and held by Bulgaria until 1246 when the Upper Vardar valley was incorporated once more into a Byzantine state – the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Nicaea" title="Empire of Nicaea">Empire of Nicaea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[73]</a></sup> Byzantine conquest was briefly reversed in 1255 by the regents of the young <a href="/wiki/Michael_Asen_I_of_Bulgaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Michael Asen I of Bulgaria">Michael Asen I of Bulgaria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[74]</a></sup> Meanwhile, in the parallel civil war for the Crown in <a href="/wiki/Veliko_Tarnovo" title="Veliko Tarnovo">Tarnovo</a> Skopje <a href="/wiki/Boyar" title="Boyar">bolyar</a> and grandson to <a href="/wiki/Stefan_Nemanja" title="Stefan Nemanja">Stefan Nemanja</a> <a href="/wiki/Constantine_Tikh_of_Bulgaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Constantine Tikh of Bulgaria">Constantine Tikh</a> gained the upper hand and ruled until Europe's only successful peasant revolt the <a href="/wiki/Uprising_of_Ivaylo" title="Uprising of Ivaylo">Uprising of Ivaylo</a> deposed him. In 1282 Skopje was captured by Serbian king <a href="/wiki/Stefan_Uro%C5%A1_II_Milutin_of_Serbia" class="mw-redirect" title="Stefan Uroš II Milutin of Serbia">Milutin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[75]</a></sup> Under the political stability of the <a href="/wiki/Nemanji%C4%87" class="mw-redirect" title="Nemanjić">Nemanjić</a> rule, Skopje slowly spread outside the walls of the fortress towards Gazi Baba hill.<sup id="cite_ref-kalemed_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kalemed-68">[65]</a></sup> Churches, monasteries and markets were built and tradesmen from <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">Venice</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dubrovnik" title="Dubrovnik">Dubrovnik</a> opened shops. The town greatly benefited from its location on the roads between <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Middle-East" class="mw-redirect" title="Middle-East">Middle-East</a> and <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>. In the 14th century, Skopje became such an important city that king <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Uro%C5%A1_IV_Du%C5%A1an_of_Serbia" class="mw-redirect" title="Stephen Uroš IV Dušan of Serbia">Dušan</a> made it the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia_(medieval)" title="Kingdom of Serbia (medieval)">Serbian kingdom</a>. In 1346, he was crowned "Emperor of the Serbs and Greeks" in Skopje.<sup id="cite_ref-history_43-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-43">[42]</a></sup> After his death the Serbian Empire collapsed into many small principalities which were unable to defend themselves against the Turks. Skopje was first inherited by the <a href="/wiki/Lordship_of_Prilep" title="Lordship of Prilep">Lordship of Prilep</a> and finally taken by <a href="/wiki/Vuk_Brankovi%C4%87" title="Vuk Branković">Vuk Branković</a> in the wake of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Maritsa" title="Battle of Maritsa">Battle of Maritsa</a> (1371)<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[76]</a></sup> before becoming part of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> in 1392.<sup id="cite_ref-history_43-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-43">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ottoman_period">Ottoman period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Ottoman period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mustafa_Pa%C5%9Fa_Mosque,_Skopje.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Mustafa_Pa%C5%9Fa_Mosque%2C_Skopje.jpg/220px-Mustafa_Pa%C5%9Fa_Mosque%2C_Skopje.jpg" width="220" height="323" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Mustafa_Pa%C5%9Fa_Mosque%2C_Skopje.jpg/330px-Mustafa_Pa%C5%9Fa_Mosque%2C_Skopje.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Mustafa_Pa%C5%9Fa_Mosque%2C_Skopje.jpg/440px-Mustafa_Pa%C5%9Fa_Mosque%2C_Skopje.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1620" data-file-height="2382" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mustafa_Pa%C5%9Fa_Mosque,_Skopje.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The 15th-century <a href="/wiki/Mustafa_Pasha_Mosque" title="Mustafa Pasha Mosque">Mustafa Pasha Mosque</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Skopje economic life greatly benefited from its position in the middle of <a href="/wiki/Rumelia" title="Rumelia">Turkish Europe</a>. Until the 17th century, Skopje experienced a long golden age. Around 1650, the number of inhabitants in Skopje was between 30,000 and 60,000 and the city contained more than 10,000 houses. It was then one of the only big cities on the territory of future <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a>, together with <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo" title="Sarajevo">Sarajevo</a>. At that time, <a href="/wiki/Dubrovnik" title="Dubrovnik">Dubrovnik</a>, which was a busy harbour, had not even 7,000 inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[77]</a></sup> Following the Ottoman conquest, the city population changed. Christians were forcibly converted to <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> or were replaced by <a href="/wiki/Turkish_people" title="Turkish people">Turks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jewish_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish people">Jews</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[78]</a></sup> At that time, Christians of Skopje were mostly non converted <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Albanian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Albanian people">Albanians</a>, but also <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ragusa" title="Republic of Ragusa">Ragusan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Armenian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Armenian people">Armenian</a> tradesmen.<sup id="cite_ref-demographic_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-demographic-82">[79]</a></sup> Ottoman Turks drastically changed the appearance of the city. They organised the <a href="/wiki/Old_Bazaar,_Skopje" title="Old Bazaar, Skopje">Bazaar</a> with its <a href="/wiki/Caravanserai" title="Caravanserai">caravanserais</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">mosques</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkish_bath" title="Turkish bath">baths</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ottoman_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ottoman-83">[80]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Shkup1912.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Shkup1912.jpg/220px-Shkup1912.jpg" width="220" height="108" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Shkup1912.jpg/330px-Shkup1912.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Shkup1912.jpg/440px-Shkup1912.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2580" data-file-height="1265" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Shkup1912.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Skopje after being captured by Albanian revolutionaries in August, 1912 after defeating the Ottoman forces holding the city</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city severely suffered from the <a href="/wiki/Great_Turkish_War" title="Great Turkish War">Great Turkish War</a> at the end of the 17th century and consequently experienced recession until the 19th century. In 1689, Austrians seized Skopje which was already weakened by a <a href="/wiki/Cholera" title="Cholera">cholera</a> epidemic.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[81]</a></sup> The same day, general <a href="/wiki/Enea_Silvio_Piccolomini_(general)" title="Enea Silvio Piccolomini (general)">Silvio Piccolomini</a> set fire to the city to end the epidemic.<sup id="cite_ref-history_43-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-43">[42]</a></sup> It is however possible that he wanted to avenge damages that Turks caused in <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a> <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Vienna" title="Battle of Vienna">in 1683</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[82]</a></sup> Skopje burned during two days.<sup id="cite_ref-Mark_Avrum_Ehrlich_2009_980_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mark_Avrum_Ehrlich_2009_980-86">[83]</a></sup> The Austrian presence in Macedonia motivated Slav uprisings. Nevertheless, Austrians left the country within the year and <a href="/wiki/Hajduk" title="Hajduk">Hajduks</a>, leaders of the uprisings, had to follow them in their retreat north of the Balkans.<sup id="cite_ref-history_43-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-43">[42]</a></sup> Some were arrested by the Turks, such as <a href="/wiki/Karposh%27s_Rebellion" class="mw-redirect" title="Karposh's Rebellion">Petar Karposh</a>, who was impaled on Skopje <a href="/wiki/Stone_Bridge_(Skopje)" title="Stone Bridge (Skopje)">Stone Bridge</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the war, Skopje was in ruins. Most of the official buildings were restored or rebuilt, but the city experienced new <a href="/wiki/Plague_(disease)" title="Plague (disease)">plague</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cholera" title="Cholera">cholera</a> epidemics and many inhabitants emigrated.<sup id="cite_ref-demographic_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-demographic-82">[79]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turkish_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman Turkish Empire">The Ottoman Turkish Empire</a> as a whole entered in recession and political decline. Many rebellions and pillages occurred in Macedonia during the 18th century, either led by Turkish outlaws, <a href="/wiki/Janissaries" title="Janissaries">Janissaries</a> or <a href="/wiki/Hajduk" title="Hajduk">Hajduks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[85]</a></sup> An estimation conducted by French officers around 1836 revealed that at that time Skopje only had around 10,000 inhabitants. It was largely overwhelmed by two towns of the present-day <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Republic of Macedonia</a>: <a href="/wiki/Bitola" title="Bitola">Bitola</a> (40,000) and <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0tip" title="Štip">Štip</a> (15–20,000).<sup id="cite_ref-population1_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-population1-89">[86]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sv._Bogorodica_Skopje_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Sv._Bogorodica_Skopje_01.jpg/220px-Sv._Bogorodica_Skopje_01.jpg" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Sv._Bogorodica_Skopje_01.jpg/330px-Sv._Bogorodica_Skopje_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Sv._Bogorodica_Skopje_01.jpg/440px-Sv._Bogorodica_Skopje_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="510" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sv._Bogorodica_Skopje_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Church of the Nativity of the Virgin Mary, built in the 19th century.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Skopje began to recover from decades of decline after 1850. At that time, the city experienced a slow but steady demographic growth, mainly due to the rural exodus of Slav Macedonians. It was also fuelled by the exodus of Muslims from <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>, which were gaining autonomy and independence from the Empire at that time.<sup id="cite_ref-history_43-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-43">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-demographic_82-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-demographic-82">[79]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Tanzimat" title="Tanzimat">Tanzimat</a> reforms, <a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">nationalism</a> arose in the Empire and in 1870 a new <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Exarchate" title="Bulgarian Exarchate">Bulgarian Church</a> was established and its separate diocese was created, based on <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_identity" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic identity">ethnic identity</a>, rather than religious principles.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[87]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (December 2015)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The Slavic population of the bishopric of Skopje voted in 1874 overwhelmingly, by 91% in favour of joining the Exarchate and became part of the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Millet" title="Bulgarian Millet">Bulgarian Millet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[88]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (December 2015)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Economic growth was permitted by the construction of the Skopje-<a href="/wiki/Salonica" class="mw-redirect" title="Salonica">Salonica</a> railway in 1873.<sup id="cite_ref-history_43-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-43">[42]</a></sup> The train station was built south of the <a href="/wiki/Vardar" title="Vardar">Vardar</a> and this contributed to the relocation of economic activities on this side of the river, which had never been urbanised before.<sup id="cite_ref-reconstruction_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reconstruction-31">[30]</a></sup> Because of the rural exodus, the share of Christians in the city population arose. Some of the newcomers became part of the local elite and helped to spread nationalist ideas<sup id="cite_ref-demographic_82-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-demographic-82">[79]</a></sup> Skopje was one of the five main centres of the <a href="/wiki/Internal_Macedonian_Revolutionary_Organization" title="Internal Macedonian Revolutionary Organization">Internal Macedonian Revolutionary Organization</a> when it organised the 1903 <a href="/wiki/Ilinden%E2%80%93Preobrazhenie_Uprising" title="Ilinden–Preobrazhenie Uprising">Ilinden uprising</a>. Its revolutionary network in Skopje region was not well-developed and the lack of weapons was a serious problem. At the outbreak of the uprising the rebel forces derailed a military train.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[89]</a></sup> On 3 and 5 August respectively, they attacked a Turkish unit guarding the bridge on the Vardar river and gave a battle in the "St. Jovan" monastery. In the next few days the band was pursued by numerous <a href="/wiki/Bashibozuk" class="mw-redirect" title="Bashibozuk">Bashibozuks</a> and moved to Bulgaria.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Skopje-couteliers_1919.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Skopje-couteliers_1919.jpg/220px-Skopje-couteliers_1919.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Skopje-couteliers_1919.jpg/330px-Skopje-couteliers_1919.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Skopje-couteliers_1919.jpg/440px-Skopje-couteliers_1919.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1061" data-file-height="696" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Skopje-couteliers_1919.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cutlers in the <a href="/wiki/Old_Bazaar,_Skopje" title="Old Bazaar, Skopje">Old Bazaar</a> around 1900.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1877, Skopje was chosen as the capital city of the new <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Vilayet" title="Kosovo Vilayet">Kosovo Vilayet</a>, which encompassed present-day <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>, northwestern Macedonia and the <a href="/wiki/Sanjak_of_Novi_Pazar" title="Sanjak of Novi Pazar">Sanjak of Novi Pazar</a>. In 1905, the city had 32,000 inhabitants, making it the largest of the vilayet, although closely followed by <a href="/wiki/Prizren" title="Prizren">Prizren</a> with its 30,000 inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-44">[43]</a></sup> Of the Skopje Muslim population of the late Ottoman period German linguist <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Weigand" title="Gustav Weigand">Gustav Weigand</a> noted that though most were Albanians regarded as <i>Turks</i> or Ottomans (Osmanli), they spoke Turkish in public and Albanian at home.<sup id="cite_ref-Hart214_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hart214-93">[90]</a></sup> At the beginning of the 20th century, local economy was focused on <a href="/wiki/Dyeing" title="Dyeing">dyeing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Weaving" title="Weaving">weaving</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tanning_(leather)" title="Tanning (leather)">tanning</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ironworks" title="Ironworks">ironworks</a> and wine and flour processing.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica_44-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-44">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Young_Turk_Revolution" title="Young Turk Revolution">Young Turk Revolution</a> in 1908, the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Turkish Empire</a> experienced democracy and several political parties were created.<sup id="cite_ref-history_43-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-43">[42]</a></sup> However, some of the policies implemented by the <a href="/wiki/Young_Turks" title="Young Turks">Young Turks</a>, such as a tax rise and the interdiction of ethnic-based political parties, discontented minorities. Albanians opposed the nationalist character of the movement and led local uprisings in 1910 and 1912. During the latter they managed to seize most of Kosovo and took Skopje on 11 August.<sup id="cite_ref-albanian_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-albanian-94">[91]</a></sup> On 18 August, the insurgents signed the Üsküb agreement which provided for the creation of an autonomous Albanian province<sup id="cite_ref-albanian_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-albanian-94">[91]</a></sup> and they were amnestied the day later.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[92]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="From_the_Balkan_Wars_to_present_day">From the Balkan Wars to present day</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: From the Balkan Wars to present day">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following an alliance contracted in 1912, <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> declared war on the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Turkish Empire</a>. Their goal was to definitely expel Turks from Europe. The <a href="/wiki/First_Balkan_War" title="First Balkan War">First Balkan War</a> started on 8 October 1912 and lasted six weeks. Serbians reached Skopje on 26 October. The Turkish forces had left the city the day before.<sup id="cite_ref-history_43-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-43">[42]</a></sup> The Serbian annexation led to the exodus of many Turks: 725 Turkish families left the city on 27 January 1913. The same year, the city population was evaluated at 37,000 by the Serbian authorities.<sup id="cite_ref-demographic_82-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-demographic-82">[79]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:PedroIEnUskub11031v.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/PedroIEnUskub11031v.jpg/220px-PedroIEnUskub11031v.jpg" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/PedroIEnUskub11031v.jpg/330px-PedroIEnUskub11031v.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/PedroIEnUskub11031v.jpg/440px-PedroIEnUskub11031v.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="731" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:PedroIEnUskub11031v.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Peter_I_of_Serbia" title="Peter I of Serbia">Peter I of Serbia</a> visiting Skopje in 1914</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1915, during the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">First World War</a>, Serbian Macedonia was invaded by Bulgaria, which captured Skopje on 22 October 1915 . Serbia, allied to the <a href="/wiki/Triple_Entente" title="Triple Entente">Triple Entente</a>, was helped by <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">Britain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, which formed the <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_Front" title="Macedonian Front">Macedonian Front</a>. Following a great Allied offensive in 1918, the <a href="/wiki/Arm%C3%A9e_fran%C3%A7aise_d%27Orient" class="mw-redirect" title="Armée française d'Orient">Armée française d'Orient</a> reached Skopje 29 September and took the city by surprise.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[93]</a></sup> After the end of the World War, Macedonia became part of the new <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia" title="Kingdom of Yugoslavia">Kingdom of Serbs, Croats, and Slovenes</a>, which became "Kingdom of Yugoslavia" in 1929.<sup id="cite_ref-history_43-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-43">[42]</a></sup> A mostly foreign <a href="/wiki/Serbs" title="Serbs">ethnic Serb</a> ruling class gained control, imposing a repression unknown under the previous Turkish rulers.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[94]</a></sup> The policies of de-Bulgarisation and assimilation were pursued.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[95]</a></sup> At that time part of the young locals, repressed by the Serbs, tried to find a separate way of ethnic Macedonian development.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[96]</a></sup> In 1931, in a move to formally decentralize the country, Skopje was named the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Vardar_Banovina" title="Vardar Banovina">Vardar Banovina</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia" title="Kingdom of Yugoslavia">Kingdom of Yugoslavia</a>. Until the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World War</a>, Skopje experienced strong economic growth, and its population increased. The city had 41,066 inhabitants in 1921, 64,807 in 1931, and 80,000 in 1941.<sup id="cite_ref-demographic_82-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-demographic-82">[79]</a></sup> Although located in an underdeveloped region, it attracted wealthy Serbs who opened businesses and contributed to the modernisation of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-colophon_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-colophon-100">[97]</a></sup> In 1941, Skopje had 45 factories, half of the industry in the whole of Macedonia.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[98]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Skopsko_Kale,_stara.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Skopsko_Kale%2C_stara.jpg/220px-Skopsko_Kale%2C_stara.jpg" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Skopsko_Kale%2C_stara.jpg/330px-Skopsko_Kale%2C_stara.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Skopsko_Kale%2C_stara.jpg/440px-Skopsko_Kale%2C_stara.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1020" data-file-height="646" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Skopsko_Kale,_stara.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The national theatre and the fortress around 1920.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1941, during the Second World War, Yugoslavia was invaded by <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>. Germans seized Skopje 8 April<sup id="cite_ref-history_43-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-43">[42]</a></sup> and left it to their Bulgarian allies on 22 April 1941.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERamet2006139_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERamet2006139-102">[99]</a></sup> To ensure bulgarisation of the society, authorities closed Serbian schools and churches and opened new schools and a higher education institute, the King Boris University.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[100]</a></sup> The 4,000 Jews of Skopje were all deported in 1943 to <a href="/wiki/Treblinka" class="mw-redirect" title="Treblinka">Treblinka</a> where almost all of them died.<sup id="cite_ref-jews_p._47_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jews_p._47-104">[101]</a></sup> Local Partisan detachments started a widespread guerrilla after the proclamation of the "Popular Republic of Macedonia" by the <a href="/wiki/Anti-fascist_Assembly_for_the_National_Liberation_of_Macedonia" title="Anti-fascist Assembly for the National Liberation of Macedonia">ASNOM</a> on 2 August 1944. Skopje was liberated on 13 November 1944 by Yugoslav Partisan units of the <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_National_Liberation_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Macedonian National Liberation Army">Macedonian National Liberation Army</a>, together with units of the newly allied <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_People%27s_Army" title="Bulgarian People's Army">Bulgarian People's Army</a> (Bulgaria having switched sides in the war <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_of_1944" title="Bulgarian coup d'état of 1944">in September</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[102]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[103]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[104]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>After <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Skopje greatly benefited from Socialist Yugoslav policies which encouraged industry and the development of Macedonian cultural institutions. Consequently, Skopje became home to a national library, a national philharmonic orchestra, a university and the Macedonian Academy. However, its post-war development was altered by the <a href="/wiki/1963_Skopje_earthquake" title="1963 Skopje earthquake">1963 earthquake</a> which occurred 26 July. Although relatively weak in magnitude, it caused enormous damage in the city and can be compared to the <a href="/wiki/1960_Agadir_earthquake" title="1960 Agadir earthquake">1960 Agadir earthquake</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[106]</a></sup> The disaster killed 1,070 people, injuring 3,300 others. 16,000 people were buried alive in ruins and 70% of the population lost their home.<sup id="cite_ref-post_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-post-30">[29]</a></sup> Many educational facilities, factories and historical buildings were destroyed.<sup id="cite_ref-reconstruction_31-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reconstruction-31">[30]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:US_army_in_Skopje_1963.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/US_army_in_Skopje_1963.jpg/220px-US_army_in_Skopje_1963.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/US_army_in_Skopje_1963.jpg/330px-US_army_in_Skopje_1963.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/da/US_army_in_Skopje_1963.jpg 2x" data-file-width="424" data-file-height="318" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:US_army_in_Skopje_1963.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
American soldiers in Skopje after the 1963 earthquake.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the earthquake, reconstruction was quick. It had a deep psychological impact on the population because neighbourhoods were split and people were relocated to new houses and buildings they were not familiar with.<sup id="cite_ref-post_30-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-post-30">[29]</a></sup> Reconstruction was finished by 1980, even if many elements were never built because funds were exhausted.<sup id="cite_ref-reconstruction_31-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reconstruction-31">[30]</a></sup> Skopje cityscape was drastically changed and the city became a true example of <a href="/wiki/Modernist_architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Modernist architecture">modernist architecture</a>. Demographic growth was very important after 1963, and Skopje had 408,100 inhabitants in 1981.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[107]</a></sup> However, during the 1980s and the 1990s, the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Republic of Macedonia</a> experienced inflation and recession and the local economy heavily suffered. The situation became better during the 2000s thanks to new investments. Many landmarks were restored and the "<a href="/wiki/Skopje_2014" title="Skopje 2014">Skopje 2014</a>" project renewed the appearance of the city centre.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Emblems">Emblems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Emblems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:112px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_arms_of_Skopje.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Coat_of_arms_of_Skopje.svg/110px-Coat_of_arms_of_Skopje.svg.png" width="110" height="117" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Coat_of_arms_of_Skopje.svg/165px-Coat_of_arms_of_Skopje.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Coat_of_arms_of_Skopje.svg/220px-Coat_of_arms_of_Skopje.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="122" data-file-height="130" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_arms_of_Skopje.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The coat of arms of Skopje.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Skopje" title="Flag of Skopje">Flag of Skopje</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Skopje" title="Coat of arms of Skopje">Coat of arms of Skopje</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Skopje" title="Flag of Skopje">Flag of Skopje</a><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[108]</a></sup> is a red banner in proportions 1:2 with a gold-coloured <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Skopje" title="Coat of arms of Skopje">coat of arms of the city</a> positioned in the upper-left corner. It is either vertical or horizontal, but the vertical version was the first to be used.<sup id="cite_ref-Flag_of_Skopje_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flag_of_Skopje-112">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p>The coat of arms of the city was adopted in the 1950s. It depicts the <a href="/wiki/Stone_Bridge_(Skopje)" title="Stone Bridge (Skopje)">Stone Bridge</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Vardar" title="Vardar">Vardar</a> river, the <a href="/wiki/Skopje_Fortress" title="Skopje Fortress">Kale Fortress</a> and the snow-capped peaks of the <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0ar_mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Šar mountains">Šar mountains</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[110]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administration">Administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Status">Status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MKD_muni_nonn(Skopje).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/MKD_muni_nonn%28Skopje%29.png/220px-MKD_muni_nonn%28Skopje%29.png" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/MKD_muni_nonn%28Skopje%29.png/330px-MKD_muni_nonn%28Skopje%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/MKD_muni_nonn%28Skopje%29.png/440px-MKD_muni_nonn%28Skopje%29.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="392" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MKD_muni_nonn(Skopje).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Greater Skopje among the <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_the_Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Municipalities of the Republic of Macedonia">municipalities of the Republic of Macedonia</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Being the capital and largest city of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Republic of Macedonia</a>, Skopje enjoys a particular status granted by law. The last revision of its status was made in 2004. Since then, the City of Skopje has been divided into 10 municipalities which all have a council and a mayor, like all the <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_the_Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Municipalities of the Republic of Macedonia">municipalities of the Republic of Macedonia</a>. Municipalities only deal with matters specific of their territory, and the City of Skopje deals with matters that concern all of them, or that cannot be divided between two or more municipalities.<sup id="cite_ref-local_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-local-114">[111]</a></sup></p>
<p>The City of Skopje is part of <a href="/wiki/Skopje_Statistical_Region" title="Skopje Statistical Region">Skopje Statistical Region</a>, which has no political or administrative power.<sup id="cite_ref-local_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-local-114">[111]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="City_Council">City Council</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: City Council">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The City Council consists of 45 members who serve a four-year term. It primarily deals with budget, global orientations and relations between the City and the government. Several commissions exist to treat more specific topics, such as urbanism, finances, environment of local development.<sup id="cite_ref-council_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-council-115">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>The President of the Council is elected by the Council Members. Since 2009 the president has been Irena Miševa, member of the <a href="/wiki/VMRO-DPMNE" title="VMRO-DPMNE">VMRO-DPMNE</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-council_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-council-115">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the 2013 local elections, the City Council is constituted as follows:<sup id="cite_ref-council_115-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-council-115">[112]</a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mayor">Mayor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Mayor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Koce_Trajanovski_cropp.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Koce_Trajanovski_cropp.jpg/180px-Koce_Trajanovski_cropp.jpg" width="180" height="358" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Koce_Trajanovski_cropp.jpg/270px-Koce_Trajanovski_cropp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f5/Koce_Trajanovski_cropp.jpg 2x" data-file-width="320" data-file-height="636" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Koce_Trajanovski_cropp.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Koce Trajanovski, Mayor of Skopje since 2009.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Mayor of Skopje is elected every four years. The current mayor has been Koce Trajanovski since 2009. A former deputy and mayor of <a href="/wiki/Gazi_Baba" class="mw-redirect" title="Gazi Baba">Gazi Baba</a> municipality, he is a member of the <a href="/wiki/VMRO-DPMNE" title="VMRO-DPMNE">VMRO-DPMNE</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>The mayor represents the City of Skopje and he can submit ideas to the Council. He manages the administrative bodies and their officials.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[114]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Municipalities">Municipalities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Municipalities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Skopje was first divided into administrative units in 1945, but the first municipalities were created in 1976. They were five: <a href="/wiki/Centar_Municipality_(Skopje)" class="mw-redirect" title="Centar Municipality (Skopje)">Centar</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C4%8Cair_municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Čair municipality">Čair</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karpo%C5%A1_municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Karpoš municipality">Karpoš</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gazi_Baba_municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Gazi Baba municipality">Gazi Baba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kisela_Voda_municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Kisela Voda municipality">Kisela Voda</a>. After the independence of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Republic of Macedonia</a>, power was centralised and municipalities lost much of their competences. A 1996 law restored them and created two new municipalities: <a href="/wiki/Gjor%C4%8De_Petrov_municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Gjorče Petrov municipality">Gjorče Petrov</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0uto_Orizari_municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Šuto Orizari municipality">Šuto Orizari</a>. After the <a href="/wiki/Insurgency_in_the_Republic_of_Macedonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Insurgency in the Republic of Macedonia">insurgency between Albanian rebels and Macedonian forces</a> in 2001, a new law was enacted in 2004 to incorporate <a href="/wiki/Saraj_municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Saraj municipality">Saraj municipality</a> into the City of Skopje. Saraj is mostly populated by Albanians and, since then, Albanians represent more than 20% of the city population. Thus Albanian became the second official language of the city administration, something which was one of the claims of the Albanian rebels. The same year, <a href="/wiki/Aerodrom_Municipality_(Skopje)" class="mw-redirect" title="Aerodrom Municipality (Skopje)">Aerodrom Municipality</a> separated itself from Kisela Voda, and <a href="/wiki/Butel_municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Butel municipality">Butel municipality</a> from Čair.<sup id="cite_ref-local_114-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-local-114">[111]</a></sup></p>
<p>Municipalities are administered by a council of 23 members elected every four years. They also have a mayor and several departments (education, culture, finances...). The mayor primarily deals with these departments.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[115]</a></sup></p>

<li><a href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_arms_of_%C5%A0uto_Orizari_Municipality.svg" class="image"><img alt="Coat of arms of Šuto Orizari Municipality.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Coat_of_arms_of_%C5%A0uto_Orizari_Municipality.svg/20px-Coat_of_arms_of_%C5%A0uto_Orizari_Municipality.svg.png" width="20" height="23" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Coat_of_arms_of_%C5%A0uto_Orizari_Municipality.svg/30px-Coat_of_arms_of_%C5%A0uto_Orizari_Municipality.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Coat_of_arms_of_%C5%A0uto_Orizari_Municipality.svg/40px-Coat_of_arms_of_%C5%A0uto_Orizari_Municipality.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="260" data-file-height="300" /></a> <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0uto_Orizari_municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Šuto Orizari municipality">Šuto Orizari</a> (<i>Шуто Оризари</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_arms_of_Karpo%C5%A1_Municipality.svg" class="image"><img alt="Coat of arms of Karpoš Municipality.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Coat_of_arms_of_Karpo%C5%A1_Municipality.svg/20px-Coat_of_arms_of_Karpo%C5%A1_Municipality.svg.png" width="20" height="23" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Coat_of_arms_of_Karpo%C5%A1_Municipality.svg/30px-Coat_of_arms_of_Karpo%C5%A1_Municipality.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Coat_of_arms_of_Karpo%C5%A1_Municipality.svg/40px-Coat_of_arms_of_Karpo%C5%A1_Municipality.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="582" data-file-height="669" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Karpo%C5%A1_municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Karpoš municipality">Karpoš</a> (<i>Карпош</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_arms_of_%C7%B4or%C4%8De_Petrov_Municipality.svg" class="image"><img alt="Coat of arms of Ǵorče Petrov Municipality.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Coat_of_arms_of_%C7%B4or%C4%8De_Petrov_Municipality.svg/20px-Coat_of_arms_of_%C7%B4or%C4%8De_Petrov_Municipality.svg.png" width="20" height="25" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Coat_of_arms_of_%C7%B4or%C4%8De_Petrov_Municipality.svg/30px-Coat_of_arms_of_%C7%B4or%C4%8De_Petrov_Municipality.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Coat_of_arms_of_%C7%B4or%C4%8De_Petrov_Municipality.svg/40px-Coat_of_arms_of_%C7%B4or%C4%8De_Petrov_Municipality.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="473" data-file-height="600" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Gjor%C4%8De_Petrov_municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Gjorče Petrov municipality">Gjorče Petrov</a> (<i>Ѓорче Петров</i>)</li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_weight">Economic weight</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Economic weight">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Skopje_X9.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Skopje_X9.JPG/220px-Skopje_X9.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Skopje_X9.JPG/330px-Skopje_X9.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Skopje_X9.JPG/440px-Skopje_X9.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Skopje_X9.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The small business district.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Skopje is a medium city at European level. Being the capital and largest city in the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Republic of Macedonia</a>, Skopje concentrates a large share of the national economy. The <a href="/wiki/Skopje_Statistical_Region" title="Skopje Statistical Region">Skopje Statistical Region</a>, which encompasses the City of Skopje and some neighbouring municipalities, produces 45,5% of the Macedonian <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[118]</a></sup> In 2009, the regional GDP per capita amounted to <a href="/wiki/American_dollar" class="mw-redirect" title="American dollar">USD</a> 6,565, or 155% of the Macedonian GDP per capita.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[119]</a></sup> This figure is however smaller than the one of <a href="/wiki/Sofia" title="Sofia">Sofia</a> (USD 10,106),<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[120]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo" title="Sarajevo">Sarajevo</a> (USD 10,048)<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[121]</a></sup> or <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a> (USD 7,983),<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[122]</a></sup> but higher than the one of <a href="/wiki/Tirana" title="Tirana">Tirana</a> (USD 4,126).<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[123]</a></sup></p>
<p>Because there are no other large cities in the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Republic of Macedonia</a>, and because of political and economical centralisation, a large number of Macedonians living outside of Skopje work in the capital city. The dynamism of the city also encourages <a href="/wiki/Rural_exodus" class="mw-redirect" title="Rural exodus">rural exodus</a>, not only from Macedonia, but also from <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> and Southern <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-quality_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-quality-127">[124]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Firms_and_activities">Firms and activities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Firms and activities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2009, Skopje had 26,056 firms but only 145 of them had a large size. The large majority of them are either small (12,017) or very small (13,625).<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[125]</a></sup> A large share of the firms deal with trade of goods (9,758), 3,839 are specialised in business and real estate, and 2,849 are manufacturers.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[126]</a></sup> Although few in number, large firms account for 51% of the local production outside finance.<sup id="cite_ref-region_39-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-region-39">[38]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Skopje_X132.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Skopje_X132.JPG/220px-Skopje_X132.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Skopje_X132.JPG/330px-Skopje_X132.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Skopje_X132.JPG/440px-Skopje_X132.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Skopje_X132.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Tobacco" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial Tobacco">Imperial Tobacco</a> plant.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city industry is dominated by food processing, textile, printing and metal processing. In 2012, it accounted for 30% of the city GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-region_39-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-region-39">[38]</a></sup> Most of the industrial areas are located in <a href="/wiki/Gazi_Baba_municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Gazi Baba municipality">Gazi Baba municipality</a>, on the major routes and rail lines to <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[127]</a></sup> Notably, the <a href="/wiki/ArcelorMittal" title="ArcelorMittal">ArcelorMittal</a> and Makstil steel plants are located there, and also the Skopje Brewery. Other zones are located between Aerodrom and Kisela Voda, along the railway to <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>. These zones comprise Alkaloid Skopje (pharmaceuticals), Rade Končar (electrical supplies), <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Tobacco" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial Tobacco">Imperial Tobacco</a>, and Ohis (fertilisers). Two <a href="/wiki/Special_economic_zone" title="Special economic zone">special economic zones</a> also exist, around the airport and the Okta refinery. They have attracted several foreign companies, such as <a href="/wiki/Johnson_Controls" title="Johnson Controls">Johnson Controls</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johnson_Matthey" title="Johnson Matthey">Johnson Matthey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Van_Hool" title="Van Hool">Van Hool</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[128]</a></sup></p>
<p>As the financial capital of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Republic of Macedonia</a>, Skopje is the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_Stock_Exchange" title="Macedonian Stock Exchange">Macedonian Stock Exchange</a>, of the <a href="/wiki/National_Bank_of_the_Republic_of_Macedonia" title="National Bank of the Republic of Macedonia">National Bank</a> and of most of the Macedonian banking, insurance and telecommunication companies, such as <a href="/wiki/Makedonski_Telekom" title="Makedonski Telekom">Makedonski Telekom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Komercijalna_banka_Skopje" title="Komercijalna banka Skopje">Komercijalna banka Skopje</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stopanska_Banka" title="Stopanska Banka">Stopanska Banka</a>. The services sector produces 60% of the city GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-region_39-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-region-39">[38]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Zeleno_pazarce_-_Flickr_-_ImogenX_(9).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Zeleno_pazarce_-_Flickr_-_ImogenX_%289%29.jpg/220px-Zeleno_pazarce_-_Flickr_-_ImogenX_%289%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Zeleno_pazarce_-_Flickr_-_ImogenX_%289%29.jpg/330px-Zeleno_pazarce_-_Flickr_-_ImogenX_%289%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Zeleno_pazarce_-_Flickr_-_ImogenX_%289%29.jpg/440px-Zeleno_pazarce_-_Flickr_-_ImogenX_%289%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1709" data-file-height="1280" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Zeleno_pazarce_-_Flickr_-_ImogenX_(9).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Zelen Pazar ("green market")</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Besides many small traditional shops, Skopje has two large markets, the "Zelen Pazar" (green market) and the "Bit Pazar" (flea market). They are both considered as local institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-thiesen57_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thiesen57-40">[39]</a></sup> However, since the 1970s, retailing has largely been modernised and Skopje now has many supermarkets and shopping malls. The largest, Skopje City Mall, opened in 2012. It comprises a <a href="/wiki/Carrefour" title="Carrefour">Carrefour</a> hypermarket, 130 shops and a cinema, and employs 2,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[129]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vero_Center.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Vero_Center.jpg/220px-Vero_Center.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Vero_Center.jpg/330px-Vero_Center.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Vero_Center.jpg/440px-Vero_Center.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="1836" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vero_Center.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mall in Skopje</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Employment">Employment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Employment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>51% of Skopje active population is employed in small firms. 52% of the population work in the services sector, 34% in industry, and the remaining is mainly employed in administration.<sup id="cite_ref-region_39-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-region-39">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>The unemployment rate for the <a href="/wiki/Skopje_Statistical_Region" title="Skopje Statistical Region">Skopje Statistical Region</a> was at 27% in 2009, three points under the national rate (30%). The neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Polog_Statistical_Region" title="Polog Statistical Region">Polog Region</a> had a similar rate, but the less affected region was the <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_Statistical_Region" title="Southwestern Statistical Region">South-West</a>, with 22%.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[130]</a></sup> Unemployment in Skopje mainly concern men, who represent 56% of job-seekers, people between 25 and 44 years old (45% of job-seekers), and non-qualified people (43%).<sup id="cite_ref-region_39-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-region-39">[38]</a></sup> Unemployment also concerns <a href="/wiki/Roma_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Roma people">Roma people</a>, who represent 4.63% of the city population. Unemployment concerns 70% of the active population in the community.<sup id="cite_ref-roma_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roma-41">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>The average net monthly wage in Skopje was at €400 in October 2010, which represented 120% of the national figure.<sup id="cite_ref-brutno_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brutno-134">[131]</a></sup> The average wage in Skopje was then lower than in <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo" title="Sarajevo">Sarajevo</a> (€522)<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[132]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sofia" title="Sofia">Sofia</a> (€436)<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[133]</a></sup> and in <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a> (€440).<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[134]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demography">Demography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Demography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ulica_Makedonija.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Ulica_Makedonija.JPG/220px-Ulica_Makedonija.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Ulica_Makedonija.JPG/330px-Ulica_Makedonija.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Ulica_Makedonija.JPG/440px-Ulica_Makedonija.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ulica_Makedonija.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
People on Macedonia street, the main pedestrian axis of the city.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The City of Skopje had 506,926 inhabitants within its administrative limits in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-stats1_1-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats1-1">[1]</a></sup> Skopje's employment area covers a large part of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Republic of Macedonia</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Veles_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Veles (city)">Veles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kumanovo" title="Kumanovo">Kumanovo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tetovo" title="Tetovo">Tetovo</a>, and totaling more than one million inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-trace_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trace-139">[136]</a></sup></p>
<p>Skopje concentrates a third of Macedonia's population and other Macedonian towns are much smaller. The second most populous municipality, <a href="/wiki/Kumanovo" title="Kumanovo">Kumanovo</a>, had 107,632 inhabitants in 2011,<sup id="cite_ref-stats_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats-119">[116]</a></sup> and an <a href="/wiki/Urban_unit" title="Urban unit">urban unit</a> of 76,272 inhabitants in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-stats1_1-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats1-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>Before the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman%E2%80%93Habsburg_wars" title="Ottoman–Habsburg wars">Austro-Turkish war</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Fire_of_Skopje_1689" title="Fire of Skopje 1689">1698 Great Fire</a>, Skopje was one of the biggest cities in the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a>, with a population estimated between 30,000 and 60,000 inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-history_43-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-43">[42]</a></sup> After the fire, it experienced a long period of decline and only had 10,000 inhabitants in 1836.<sup id="cite_ref-population1_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-population1-89">[86]</a></sup> However, the population started to rise again after 1850 and reached 32,000 inhabitants in 1905.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica_44-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-44">[43]</a></sup> In the 20th century, Skopje was one of the fastest growing cities in <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a> and it has 448,200 inhabitants in 1971. Since then, the demographic growth has continued at a steady pace.<sup id="cite_ref-jasna_138-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jasna-138">[135]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="wikitable" style="border-spacing: 1px; text-align:center; align:right">
