<p>Skopje, as the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Republic of Macedonia</a> as a whole, is characterised by a large ethnic diversity. The city is located in a region where Ethnic Albanians and Macedonians meet, and it welcomed Romani, Turks, Jews and Serbs throughout its history. Skopje was mainly a Muslim city until the 19th century, when large number of Christians started to settle there. According to the 2002 census, Macedonians were the largest ethnic group in Skopje, with 338,358 inhabitants, or 66.75% of the population. Then came Albanians with 103,891 inhabitants (20.49%), Roma people with 23,475 (4.63%), Serbs (14,298 inhabitants), Turks (8,595), Bosniaks (7,585) and Vlachs (2,557). 8,167 people did not belong to any of these groups.<sup id="cite_ref-stats1_1-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats1-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ethnic Macedonians form an overwhelming majority of the population in the municipalities of <a href="/wiki/Aerodrom_Municipality_(Skopje)" class="mw-redirect" title="Aerodrom Municipality (Skopje)">Aerodrom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Centar_Municipality_(Skopje)" class="mw-redirect" title="Centar Municipality (Skopje)">Centar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gjor%C4%8De_Petrov_municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Gjorče Petrov municipality">Gjorče Petrov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karpo%C5%A1_municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Karpoš municipality">Karpoš</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kisela_Voda_municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Kisela Voda municipality">Kisela Voda</a>, which are all located south of the <a href="/wiki/Vardar" title="Vardar">Vardar</a>. They also form a majority in <a href="/wiki/Butel_municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Butel municipality">Butel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gazi_Baba_municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Gazi Baba municipality">Gazi Baba</a> which are north of the river. Albanians form a majority in <a href="/wiki/%C4%8Cair_municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Čair municipality">Čair</a> which roughly corresponds to the <a href="/wiki/Old_Bazaar,_Skopje" title="Old Bazaar, Skopje">Old Bazaar</a>, and in <a href="/wiki/Saraj_municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Saraj municipality">Saraj</a>. They form a large minority in Butel and Gazi Baba. <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0uto_Orizari_municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Šuto Orizari municipality">Šuto Orizari</a>, located on the northern edge of the city, is predominantly Roma.<sup id="cite_ref-stats1_1-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats1-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>When an ethnic minority forms at least 20% of the population in a municipality, its language can become official on the local level. Thus, in Čair and Saraj schools and administration use Albanian, and Romani in Šuto Orizari.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[137]</a></sup> The latter is the only municipality in the world where Romani is an official language.<sup id="cite_ref-roma_41-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roma-41">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>Relations between the two largest groups, Macedonians and Albanians, are sometimes difficult, as in the rest of the country. Each group tolerate the other but they tend to avoid each other and live in what can appear as two parallel worlds.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[138]</a></sup> The Roma minority is on its side very deprived. Its exact size is not known because many Macedonian Roma declare themselves as belonging to other ethnic groups or simply avoid censuses. However, even if official figures are underestimated, Skopje is the city in the world with the largest Roma population.<sup id="cite_ref-roma_41-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roma-41">[40]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Presveta_Bogordica_od_Skopje_4.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Presveta_Bogordica_od_Skopje_4.JPG/220px-Presveta_Bogordica_od_Skopje_4.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Presveta_Bogordica_od_Skopje_4.JPG/330px-Presveta_Bogordica_od_Skopje_4.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Presveta_Bogordica_od_Skopje_4.JPG/440px-Presveta_Bogordica_od_Skopje_4.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Presveta_Bogordica_od_Skopje_4.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The church of the Nativity of the Virgin Mary.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Religious affiliation is diverse: Macedonians, Serbs and Vlachs are mainly Orthodox, while Albanians, Turks and Roma (Gypsies) are usually Muslim, although there exists an almost equal amount of Orthodox Romani. Skopje also has a Catholic Albanian minority, to which belonged <a href="/wiki/Mother_Teresa" title="Mother Teresa">Mother Teresa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the 2002 census, 68.5% of the population of Skopje belonged to the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Church</a>, while 28.6% of it belonged to <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>. The city also had a <a href="/wiki/Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic">Catholic</a> (0.5%) and <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a> (0.04%) minorities.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[140]</a></sup> The Catholics are served by the Latin <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Skopje" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Skopje">bishopric of Skopje</a>, in which is also vested the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Catholic_Apostolic_Exarchate_of_Macedonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Byzantine Catholic Apostolic Exarchate of Macedonia">Byzantine Catholic Apostolic Exarchate of Macedonia</a>.</p>
<p>Until <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Skopje had a significant <a href="/wiki/Jew" class="mw-redirect" title="Jew">Jewish</a> minority which mainly descended from Spanish <a href="/wiki/Sephardi_Jews" title="Sephardi Jews">Sephardis</a> who had escaped the <a href="/wiki/Inquisition" title="Inquisition">Inquisition</a>. The community comprised 2,424 members in 1939 and most of them were deported and killed by <a href="/wiki/Nazis" class="mw-redirect" title="Nazis">Nazis</a>. After the war, most of the survivors settled in <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Mark_Avrum_Ehrlich_2009_980_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mark_Avrum_Ehrlich_2009_980-86">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[141]</a></sup></p>
<p>Because of its Ottoman past, Skopje has more <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">mosques</a> than <a href="/wiki/Church_(building)" title="Church (building)">churches</a>. Religious communities often complain about the lack of infrastructure and new places of worship are often built.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[142]</a></sup> Skopje is the seat of many Macedonian religious organisations, such as the <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_Orthodox_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Macedonian Orthodox Church">Macedonian Orthodox Church</a> and the Islamic Religious Union of Macedonia. It has an Orthodox cathedral and seminary, several <a href="/wiki/Madrasah" class="mw-redirect" title="Madrasah">madrasahs</a>, a Roman Catholic cathedral and a <a href="/wiki/Synagogue" title="Synagogue">synagogue</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[143]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Skopje has several public and private hospitals and specialised medical institutions, such as a psychiatric hospital, two obstetric hospitals, a gerontology hospital and institutes for respiratory and ocular diseases.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[144]</a></sup> In 2012, Skopje had a ratio of one physician per 251.6 inhabitants, a figure higher than the national ratio (one per 370.9). The ratio of medical specialists was also higher than in the rest of the country. However, the ratio of hospital beds, pharmacists and dentists was lower in Skopje.<sup id="cite_ref-health_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-health-148">[145]</a></sup> The population in Skopje enjoys better health standards than other Macedonians. In 2010, the mortality rate was at 8.6‰ in Skopje and 9.3‰ on the national level. The infant mortality rate was at 6.8‰ in Skopje and 7.6‰ in Macedonia.<sup id="cite_ref-health_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-health-148">[145]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9D%D0%A3%D0%91%D0%A1%D0%9A-%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%B4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/%D0%9D%D0%A3%D0%91%D0%A1%D0%9A-%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%B4.jpg/220px-%D0%9D%D0%A3%D0%91%D0%A1%D0%9A-%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%B4.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/%D0%9D%D0%A3%D0%91%D0%A1%D0%9A-%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%B4.jpg/330px-%D0%9D%D0%A3%D0%91%D0%A1%D0%9A-%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%B4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/%D0%9D%D0%A3%D0%91%D0%A1%D0%9A-%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%B4.jpg/440px-%D0%9D%D0%A3%D0%91%D0%A1%D0%9A-%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%B4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="787" data-file-height="524" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9D%D0%A3%D0%91%D0%A1%D0%9A-%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%B4.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/National_and_University_Library_%22St._Kliment_of_Ohrid%22" title="National and University Library &quot;St. Kliment of Ohrid&quot;">St Clement of Ohrid National and University Library</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Skopje's citizenry is generally more educated than the rest of the country. For one, 16% of Skopjans graduated university in contrast to 10% for the rest of the country. The amount of people with a complete lack of education or ones who received a partial education is lower in Skopje at 9% compared to the provincial average of 17%. 80% of Macedonian citizens who hold a <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Philosophy" title="Doctor of Philosophy">PhD</a> take up residence in Skopje.<sup id="cite_ref-strategija_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-strategija-149">[146]</a></sup></p>
<p>Skopje has 21 secondary schools; 5 of which serve as general high-school gymnasiums and 16 vocational schools.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[147]</a></sup> The city is also host to several higher education institutions, the most notable of which is <a href="/wiki/Ss._Cyril_and_Methodius_University_of_Skopje" title="Ss. Cyril and Methodius University of Skopje">Ss. Cyril and Methodius University</a>, founded in 1949. The university has 23 departments, 10 research institutes and is attended by an average of 50,000 students.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[148]</a></sup> After the declaration of independence for the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Republic of Macedonia</a> in 1991, several private universities were brought to existence. The largest private universities in Skopje are currently <a href="/wiki/European_University-Republic_of_Macedonia" title="European University-Republic of Macedonia">European University</a> with 7 departments<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[149]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/FON_University" title="FON University">FON University</a> with 9 departments respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[150]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Skopje_X127.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Skopje_X127.JPG/200px-Skopje_X127.JPG" width="200" height="299" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Skopje_X127.JPG/300px-Skopje_X127.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Skopje_X127.JPG/400px-Skopje_X127.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="3872" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Skopje_X127.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/MRT_Center" title="MRT Center">Macedonian Radio-Television headquarters</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Skopje is the largest media center in Macedonia. Of the 818 newspapers surveyed in 2000 by the Ministry of Information, over 600 had their headquarters in Skopje. The daily <a href="/wiki/Dnevnik_(Skopje)" title="Dnevnik (Skopje)">Dnevnik</a>, founded in 1996, with 60 000 runs per day is the most printed in the country. Also based in Skopje, <a href="/wiki/Ve%C4%8Der_(Macedonia)" title="Večer (Macedonia)">Večer</a> is pulled 50,000 copies and the state owns one third of its capital, as well as <a href="/wiki/Nova_Makedonija" title="Nova Makedonija">Nova Makedonija</a>, reprinted 20,000 copies. Other major newspapers in Skopje, totally private, are Utrinski Vesnik (30,000 copies), Vest (25,000 copies) and <a href="/wiki/Vreme_(newspaper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Vreme (newspaper)">Vreme</a> (15,000 copies). Magazines Fokus (12,000 copies), Start (10,000 copies), and Denes (7,500 copies) also have their headquarters in Skopje.<sup id="cite_ref-media_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-media-154">[151]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[152]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city is home of the studios of <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_Radio-Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Macedonian Radio-Television">Macedonian Radio-Television (MRT)</a>, the country's public radio and television. Founded in 1966, it operate withs three national broadcast channels, twenty-four hours at day. The most popular private television stations are <a href="/wiki/Sitel_(TV_channel)" title="Sitel (TV channel)">Sitel</a>. <a href="/wiki/Kanal_5_(Macedonia)" title="Kanal 5 (Macedonia)">Kanal 5</a>, Telma, Alfa TV and AlsatM are another major private television companies.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[153]</a></sup> MRT also operates radio stations with national coverage, the private station Skopje's Kanal 77 is the only one to have such a span. Radio <a href="/wiki/Antenna_5_FM" title="Antenna 5 FM">Antenna 5</a> and Metropolis are two other major private stations that have their headquarters in Skopje.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[154]</a></sup></p>
<p>Also, the city boasts big news agencies in the country, both public, as the <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_Information_Agency" title="Macedonian Information Agency">Macedonian Information Agency</a>, and private, such as the <a href="/wiki/Makfax" title="Makfax">Makfax</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-media_154-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-media-154">[151]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_Skopje" class="mw-redirect" title="Sports in Skopje">Sports in Skopje</a></div>
<p>As the capital and largest city of Macedonia, Skopje has many major sporting facilities. The city has three large swimming pools, two of which feature Olympic pools. These pools are particularly relevant to coaching water polo teams. Skopje also boasts many football stadiums, like Ilinden in Čair and Železarnica, which can accommodate between 4,000 and 4,500 spectators. The basketball court Kale can accommodate 5 000 people and the court of Jane Sandanski, 4000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[155]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Skopje_X126.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Skopje_X126.JPG/220px-Skopje_X126.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Skopje_X126.JPG/330px-Skopje_X126.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Skopje_X126.JPG/440px-Skopje_X126.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Skopje_X126.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_Arena" title="Philip II Arena">Philip II Arena</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The largest stadium remains the <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_Arena" title="Philip II Arena">Philip II Arena</a>. The stadium, built in 1947 and named until 2008, City Stadium Skopje<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[156]</a></sup> experienced a total renovation, begun in 2009 to meet the standards of FIFA. Fully renovated the stadium contains 32,580 seats,<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[157]</a></sup> and a health spa and fitness. The <a href="/wiki/Boris_Trajkovski_Sports_Center" title="Boris Trajkovski Sports Center">Boris Trajkovski Sports Center</a> is the largest sports complex in the country. It was opened in 2008 and named after president <a href="/wiki/Boris_Trajkovski" title="Boris Trajkovski">Boris Trajkovski</a>, who died in 2004. It includes room dedicated to handball, basketball and volleyball, a bowling alley, a fitness area and an ice hockey court. Its main hall, which regularly hosts concerts, holds around 10,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[158]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/FK_Vardar" title="FK Vardar">FK Vardar</a> and <a href="/wiki/FK_Rabotni%C4%8Dki" title="FK Rabotnički">FK Rabotnički</a> are the two most popular football teams, playing in the first national league. Their workouts are held at Philip II Arena, like those of the national team. The city is also home to many smaller football clubs, such as: <a href="/wiki/FK_Makedonija_Gjor%C4%8De_Petrov" title="FK Makedonija Gjorče Petrov">FK Makedonija Gjorče Petrov</a>, <a href="/wiki/FK_Gorno_Lisi%C4%8De" title="FK Gorno Lisiče">FK Gorno Lisiče</a>, <a href="/wiki/FK_Lokomotiva_Skopje" title="FK Lokomotiva Skopje">FK Lokomotiva Skopje</a>, <a href="/wiki/FK_Metalurg_Skopje" title="FK Metalurg Skopje">FK Metalurg Skopje</a>, <a href="/wiki/FK_Mad%C5%BEari_Solidarnost" title="FK Madžari Solidarnost">FK Madžari Solidarnost</a> and <a href="/wiki/FK_Skopje" title="FK Skopje">FK Skopje</a>, who play in first, second or third national league. Another popular sport in Macedonia is basketball, represented in particular by the teams <a href="/wiki/KK_Rabotni%C4%8Dki" title="KK Rabotnički">Rabotnički</a> and <a href="/wiki/KK_MZT_Skopje" title="KK MZT Skopje">MZT Skopje</a>. Handball is illustrated by <a href="/wiki/RK_Vardar" title="RK Vardar">RK Vardar PRO</a> and <a href="/wiki/RK_Metalurg_Skopje" title="RK Metalurg Skopje">RK Metalurg Skopje</a>, also the women's team <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDRK_Metalurg" title="ŽRK Metalurg">ŽRK Metalurg</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDRK_Vardar" class="mw-redirect" title="ŽRK Vardar">ŽRK Vardar</a>. The city co-hosted the <a href="/wiki/2008_European_Women%27s_Handball_Championship" title="2008 European Women's Handball Championship">2008 European Women's Handball Championship</a> together with <a href="/wiki/Ohrid" title="Ohrid">Ohrid</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[159]</a></sup> and will host the <a href="/wiki/2017_UEFA_Super_Cup" title="2017 UEFA Super Cup">2017 UEFA Super Cup</a>, the match between the two giants of the European football <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid" class="mw-redirect" title="Real Madrid">Real Madrid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester United">Manchester United</a></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_connections">Main connections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Main connections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:E65_Skopje_Northern_Bypass_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/E65_Skopje_Northern_Bypass_1.jpg/220px-E65_Skopje_Northern_Bypass_1.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/E65_Skopje_Northern_Bypass_1.jpg/330px-E65_Skopje_Northern_Bypass_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/E65_Skopje_Northern_Bypass_1.jpg/440px-E65_Skopje_Northern_Bypass_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:E65_Skopje_Northern_Bypass_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Skopje bypass.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Skopje is located near three other capital cities, <a href="/wiki/Prishtina" class="mw-redirect" title="Prishtina">Prishtina</a> (87 kilometres (54 miles) away), <a href="/wiki/Tirana" title="Tirana">Tirana</a> (291&#160;km) and <a href="/wiki/Sofia" title="Sofia">Sofia</a> (245&#160;km). <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a> is 233 kilometres (145 miles) south and <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a> is 433 kilometres (269 miles) north.<sup id="cite_ref-rimed_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rimed-163">[160]</a></sup> Skopje is also at the crossroad of two <a href="/wiki/Pan-European_corridors" title="Pan-European corridors">Pan-European corridors</a>: <a href="/wiki/Pan-European_Corridor_X" title="Pan-European Corridor X">Corridor X</a>, which runs between <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pan-European_Corridor_VIII" title="Pan-European Corridor VIII">Corridor VIII</a>, which runs from the <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_sea" class="mw-redirect" title="Adriatic sea">Adriatic</a> in <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Black_sea" class="mw-redirect" title="Black sea">Black sea</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>. Corridor X links Skopje to Thessaloniki, Belgrade and Western Europe, while Corridor VIII links it with Tirana and Sofia.</p>
<p>Corridor X locally corresponds to the <a href="/wiki/M-1_motorway_(Republic_of_Macedonia)" title="M-1 motorway (Republic of Macedonia)">M-1 motorway</a> (<a href="/wiki/European_route_E75" title="European route E75">E75</a>), which is the longest Macedonian highway. It also corresponds to the <a href="/wiki/Tabanovce" title="Tabanovce">Tabanovce</a>-<a href="/wiki/Gevgelija" title="Gevgelija">Gevgelija</a> railway. Corridor VIII, less developed, corresponds to the M-4 motorway and the <a href="/wiki/Ki%C4%8Devo" title="Kičevo">Kičevo</a>-Beljakovce railway. Skopje is not quite on the Corridor X and the M-1 does not pass on the city territory. Thus the junction between the M-1 and M-4 is located some 20 kilometres (12 miles) east, close to the airport. Although Skopje is geographically close to other major cities, movement of people and goods is not optimised, especially with <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>. This is mainly due to poor infrastructure. As a result, 61.8% of Skopjans have never been to <a href="/wiki/Tirana" title="Tirana">Tirana</a>, while only 6.7% have never been to <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a> and 0% to <a href="/wiki/Sofia" title="Sofia">Sofia</a>. Furthermore, 26% of Thessalonians, 33% of Sofians and 37% of Tiranans have never been to Skopje.<sup id="cite_ref-rimed_163-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rimed-163">[160]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail_and_coach_stations">Rail and coach stations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Rail and coach stations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Skopje_Train_Station_from_Mount_Vodno.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Skopje_Train_Station_from_Mount_Vodno.JPG/220px-Skopje_Train_Station_from_Mount_Vodno.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Skopje_Train_Station_from_Mount_Vodno.JPG/330px-Skopje_Train_Station_from_Mount_Vodno.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Skopje_Train_Station_from_Mount_Vodno.JPG/440px-Skopje_Train_Station_from_Mount_Vodno.JPG 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="533" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Skopje_Train_Station_from_Mount_Vodno.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Main railway station as seen from Mount <a href="/wiki/Vodno" title="Vodno">Vodno</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The main railway station in Skopje is serviced by the <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a>-<a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a> and Skopje-<a href="/wiki/Prishtina" class="mw-redirect" title="Prishtina">Prishtina</a> international lines.<sup id="cite_ref-mz_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mz-164">[161]</a></sup> After the completion of the <a href="/wiki/Pan-European_Corridor_VIII" title="Pan-European Corridor VIII">Corridor VIII</a> railway scheduled for 2022, the city will also be linked to <a href="/wiki/Tirana" title="Tirana">Tirana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sofia" title="Sofia">Sofia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[162]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[163]</a></sup> Daily trains also link Skopje with other Macedonian towns, such as <a href="/wiki/Kumanovo" title="Kumanovo">Kumanovo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ki%C4%8Devo" title="Kičevo">Kičevo</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0tip" title="Štip">Štip</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bitola" title="Bitola">Bitola</a> or <a href="/wiki/Veles_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Veles (city)">Veles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mz_164-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mz-164">[161]</a></sup></p>
<p>Skopje has several minor railway stations but the city does not have its own railway network and they are only serviced by intercity or international lines. On the railway linking the main station to Belgrade and Thessaloniki are Dračevo and Dolno Lisiče stations, and on the railway to Kičevo are Skopje-North, Gjorče Petrov and Saraj stations. Several other stations are freight-only.<sup id="cite_ref-stations_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stations-167">[164]</a></sup></p>
<p>Skopje coach station opened in 2005 and is built right under the main railway station. It can host 450 coaches in a day.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[165]</a></sup> Coach connections to and from Skopje are much more efficient and diverse than train connections. Indeed, it is regularly linked to many Macedonian localities and foreign cities including <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sofia" title="Sofia">Sofia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[166]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transport">Public transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Public transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Skopje_X32.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Skopje_X32.JPG/220px-Skopje_X32.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Skopje_X32.JPG/330px-Skopje_X32.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Skopje_X32.JPG/440px-Skopje_X32.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Skopje_X32.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A red double-decker bus in Skopje.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Skopje has a bus network managed by the city and operated by three companies. The oldest and largest is JSP Skopje, a public company founded in 1948. JSP lost its monopoly on public transport in 1990 and two new companies, Sloboda Prevoz and Mak Ekspres, obtained several lines. However, most of the network is still in the hands of JSP which operates 67 lines on 80. Only 24 lines are urban, the others serving localities around the city.<sup id="cite_ref-transpower_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-transpower-170">[167]</a></sup> Many of the JSP buses are (by Chinese buse builder <a href="/wiki/Yutong" title="Yutong">Yutong</a>) red <a href="/wiki/Double-decker_bus" title="Double-decker bus">double-decker buses</a> designed to look like the British-made buses that were in use in the 1950s and 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[168]</a></sup></p>
<p>A tram network has long been planned in Skopje and the idea was first proposed in the 1980s. The project became real in 2006 when the mayor Trifun Kostovski asked for feasibility studies. His successor Koce Trajanovski launched a call for tenders in 2010 and the first line is scheduled for 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[169]</a></sup></p>
<p>A new network for small buses started to operate in June 2014, not to replace but to decrease the number of big buses in the city centre.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airport">Airport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Airport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Skopje_Alexander_the_Great_Airport.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Skopje_Alexander_the_Great_Airport.jpg/220px-Skopje_Alexander_the_Great_Airport.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Skopje_Alexander_the_Great_Airport.jpg/330px-Skopje_Alexander_the_Great_Airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Skopje_Alexander_the_Great_Airport.jpg/440px-Skopje_Alexander_the_Great_Airport.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1972" data-file-height="1479" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Skopje_Alexander_the_Great_Airport.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The airport</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Skopje has an international airport, <a href="/wiki/Skopje_%22Alexander_the_Great%22_Airport" title="Skopje &quot;Alexander the Great&quot; Airport">Skopje "Alexander the Great" Airport</a>. It is located in <a href="/wiki/Petrovec" class="mw-redirect" title="Petrovec">Petrovec</a>, some 20 kilometres (12 miles) east of the city. Since 2008, it has been managed by the Turkish <a href="/wiki/TAV_Airports_Holding" title="TAV Airports Holding">TAV Airports Holding</a> and it can accommodate up to four million passengers per year.<sup id="cite_ref-tav_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tav-173">[170]</a></sup> The annual traffic has constantly risen since 2008, reaching one million passengers in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[171]</a></sup></p>
<p>Skopje airport has connections to several European cities, including <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich" title="Zürich">Zürich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>. It also maintains a direct connection with <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[172]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_institutions">Cultural institutions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Cultural institutions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Skopje,_Daut_Pasuv_hamam_(turecke_lazne)_ve_Skopji,_bila_budova_v.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Skopje%2C_Daut_Pasuv_hamam_%28turecke_lazne%29_ve_Skopji%2C_bila_budova_v.jpg/220px-Skopje%2C_Daut_Pasuv_hamam_%28turecke_lazne%29_ve_Skopji%2C_bila_budova_v.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Skopje%2C_Daut_Pasuv_hamam_%28turecke_lazne%29_ve_Skopji%2C_bila_budova_v.jpg/330px-Skopje%2C_Daut_Pasuv_hamam_%28turecke_lazne%29_ve_Skopji%2C_bila_budova_v.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Skopje%2C_Daut_Pasuv_hamam_%28turecke_lazne%29_ve_Skopji%2C_bila_budova_v.jpg/440px-Skopje%2C_Daut_Pasuv_hamam_%28turecke_lazne%29_ve_Skopji%2C_bila_budova_v.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Skopje,_Daut_Pasuv_hamam_(turecke_lazne)_ve_Skopji,_bila_budova_v.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Macedonian Opera and Ballet.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Being the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Republic of Macedonia</a>, Skopje is home to the largest cultural institutions of the country, such as the <a href="/wiki/National_and_University_Library_%22St._Kliment_of_Ohrid%22" title="National and University Library &quot;St. Kliment of Ohrid&quot;">National and University Library "St. Kliment of Ohrid"</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_Academy_of_Sciences_and_Arts" title="Macedonian Academy of Sciences and Arts">Macedonian Academy of Sciences and Arts</a>, the National Theatre, the National Philarmonic Orchestra and the Macedonian Opera and Ballet. Among the local institutions are the Brothers Miladinov Library which has more than a million documents, the Cultural Information Centre which manages festivals, exhibitions and concerts, and the House of Culture Kočo Racin which is dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_art" title="Contemporary art">contemporary art</a> and young talents.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[173]</a></sup></p>
<p>Skopje has also several foreign cultural centres, such as a <a href="/wiki/Goethe-Institut" title="Goethe-Institut">Goethe-Institut</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[174]</a></sup> a <a href="/wiki/British_Council" title="British Council">British Council</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[175]</a></sup> an <a href="/wiki/Alliance_fran%C3%A7aise" class="mw-redirect" title="Alliance française">Alliance française</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[176]</a></sup> an <a href="/wiki/American_Corner" class="mw-redirect" title="American Corner">American Corner</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[177]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city has several theatres and concert halls. The Univerzalna Sala, seating 1,570, was built in 1966 and is used for concerts, fashion shows and congresses. The Metropolis Arena, designed for large concerts, has 3,546 seats. Other large halls include the Macedonian Opera and Ballet (800 seats), the National Theatre (724), and the Drama Theatre (333).<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[178]</a></sup> Other smaller venues exist, such as the Albanian Theatre and the Youth Theatre. A Turkish Theatre and a Philharmonic hall are under construction.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[179]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[180]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Museum_of_the_Macedonian_Struggle.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Museum_of_the_Macedonian_Struggle.jpg/220px-Museum_of_the_Macedonian_Struggle.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Museum_of_the_Macedonian_Struggle.jpg/330px-Museum_of_the_Macedonian_Struggle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Museum_of_the_Macedonian_Struggle.jpg/440px-Museum_of_the_Macedonian_Struggle.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="2432" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Museum_of_the_Macedonian_Struggle.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Museum_of_the_Macedonian_Struggle_(Skopje)" title="Museum of the Macedonian Struggle (Skopje)">Museum of the Macedonian Struggle</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The largest museum in Skopje is the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Macedonia" title="Museum of Macedonia">Museum of Macedonia</a> which details the history of the country. Its <a href="/wiki/Icon" title="Icon">icons</a> and lapidary collections are particularly rich.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[181]</a></sup> The Macedonian Archeological Museum, opened in 2014, keeps some of the best archeological finds in Macedonia, dating from <a href="/wiki/Prehistory" title="Prehistory">Prehistory</a> to the Ottoman period. The <a href="/wiki/National_Gallery_of_Macedonia" title="National Gallery of Macedonia">National Gallery of Macedonia</a> exhibits paintings dating from the 14th to the 20th century in two former <a href="/wiki/Turkish_baths" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish baths">Turkish baths</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Old_Bazaar,_Skopje" title="Old Bazaar, Skopje">Old Bazaar</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_Art_Museum_of_Macedonia" title="Contemporary Art Museum of Macedonia">Contemporary Art Museum of Macedonia</a> was built after the 1963 earthquake thanks to international assistance. Its collections include Macedonian and foreign art, with works by <a href="/wiki/Fernand_L%C3%A9ger" title="Fernand Léger">Fernand Léger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Masson" title="André Masson">André Masson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Picasso" title="Pablo Picasso">Pablo Picasso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hans_Hartung" title="Hans Hartung">Hans Hartung</a>, <a href="/wiki/Victor_Vasarely" title="Victor Vasarely">Victor Vasarely</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Calder" title="Alexander Calder">Alexander Calder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Soulages" title="Pierre Soulages">Pierre Soulages</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Burri" title="Alberto Burri">Alberto Burri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christo" class="mw-redirect" title="Christo">Christo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[182]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Skopje_City_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="Skopje City Museum">Skopje City Museum</a> is located inside the remains of the old train station, destroyed by the 1963 earthquake. It is dedicated to the local history and it has four departments: archeology, ethnology, history and art history.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[183]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Memorial_House_of_Mother_Teresa" title="Memorial House of Mother Teresa">Memorial House of Mother Teresa</a> was built in 2009 on the site where stood the church were the Saint was baptised.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[184]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_the_Macedonian_Struggle_(Skopje)" title="Museum of the Macedonian Struggle (Skopje)">Museum of the Macedonian Struggle</a> is dedicated to the modern national history and the struggle of Macedonians for their independence. Nearby is the <a href="/wiki/Holocaust_Memorial_Center_for_the_Jews_of_Macedonia" title="Holocaust Memorial Center for the Jews of Macedonia">Holocaust Memorial Center for the Jews of Macedonia</a>. The Macedonian Museum of Natural History showcases some 4,000 items<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[185]</a></sup> while the 12-ha <a href="/wiki/Skopje_Zoo" title="Skopje Zoo">Skopje Zoo</a> is home to 300 animals.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[186]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Skupi_(Colonia_Flavia_Scupinorum)_-_by_Pudelek_1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Skupi_%28Colonia_Flavia_Scupinorum%29_-_by_Pudelek_1.JPG/220px-Skupi_%28Colonia_Flavia_Scupinorum%29_-_by_Pudelek_1.JPG" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Skupi_%28Colonia_Flavia_Scupinorum%29_-_by_Pudelek_1.JPG/330px-Skupi_%28Colonia_Flavia_Scupinorum%29_-_by_Pudelek_1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Skupi_%28Colonia_Flavia_Scupinorum%29_-_by_Pudelek_1.JPG/440px-Skupi_%28Colonia_Flavia_Scupinorum%29_-_by_Pudelek_1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2420" data-file-height="1589" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Skupi_(Colonia_Flavia_Scupinorum)_-_by_Pudelek_1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ruins of Roman <a href="/wiki/Scupi" title="Scupi">Scupi</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Although Skopje has been destroyed many times through its history, it still has many historical landmarks which reflect the successive occupations of the city. Skopje has one of the biggest Ottoman urban complexes in Europe, with many Ottoman monuments still serving their original purpose. It was also a ground for <a href="/wiki/Modernist_architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Modernist architecture">modernist</a> experiments in the 20th century, following the 1963 earthquake. In the beginning of the 21st century, it is again the subject of massive building campaigns, thanks to the "<a href="/wiki/Skopje_2014" title="Skopje 2014">Skopje 2014</a>" project. Skopje is thus an environment where old, new, progressist, reactionary, eastern and western perspectives coexist.<sup id="cite_ref-colophon_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-colophon-100">[97]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Skopje_(%D0%A1%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BF%D1%98%D0%B5,_Shkupi)_-_aqueduct.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Skopje_%28%D0%A1%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BF%D1%98%D0%B5%2C_Shkupi%29_-_aqueduct.JPG/220px-Skopje_%28%D0%A1%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BF%D1%98%D0%B5%2C_Shkupi%29_-_aqueduct.JPG" width="220" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Skopje_%28%D0%A1%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BF%D1%98%D0%B5%2C_Shkupi%29_-_aqueduct.JPG/330px-Skopje_%28%D0%A1%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BF%D1%98%D0%B5%2C_Shkupi%29_-_aqueduct.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Skopje_%28%D0%A1%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BF%D1%98%D0%B5%2C_Shkupi%29_-_aqueduct.JPG/440px-Skopje_%28%D0%A1%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BF%D1%98%D0%B5%2C_Shkupi%29_-_aqueduct.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3436" data-file-height="2007" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Skopje_(%D0%A1%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BF%D1%98%D0%B5,_Shkupi)_-_aqueduct.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Skopje_Aqueduct" title="Skopje Aqueduct">Skopje Aqueduct</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Skopje has some remains of Prehistorical architecture which can be seen on the <a href="/wiki/Tumba_Mad%C5%BEari" title="Tumba Madžari">Tumba Madžari</a> Neolithic site.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[187]</a></sup> On the other side of the city lie the remains of the ancient <a href="/wiki/Scupi" title="Scupi">Scupi</a>, with ruins of a theatre, thermae and a basilica.<sup id="cite_ref-archeology_56-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-archeology-56">[53]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Skopje_Aqueduct" title="Skopje Aqueduct">Skopje Aqueduct</a>, located between Scupi and the city centre, is rather mysterious because its date of construction is unknown. It seems to have been built by the Byzantines or the Turks, but it was already out of use in the 16th century.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[188]</a></sup> It consists of 50 arches, worked in cloisonné masonry.<sup id="cite_ref-strategic_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-strategic-192">[189]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Manastir_sveti_Pantelejmon_vo_selo_Nerezi.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Manastir_sveti_Pantelejmon_vo_selo_Nerezi.jpg/220px-Manastir_sveti_Pantelejmon_vo_selo_Nerezi.jpg" width="220" height="189" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Manastir_sveti_Pantelejmon_vo_selo_Nerezi.jpg/330px-Manastir_sveti_Pantelejmon_vo_selo_Nerezi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Manastir_sveti_Pantelejmon_vo_selo_Nerezi.jpg/440px-Manastir_sveti_Pantelejmon_vo_selo_Nerezi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3322" data-file-height="2847" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Manastir_sveti_Pantelejmon_vo_selo_Nerezi.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Church_of_St._Panteleimon_(Gorno_Nerezi)" title="Church of St. Panteleimon (Gorno Nerezi)">Church of St. Panteleimon</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Skopje_Fortress" title="Skopje Fortress">Skopje Fortress</a> was rebuilt several times before it was destroyed by the 1963 earthquake. Since then, it has been restored to its medieval appearance. It is the only medieval monument in Skopje, but several churches located around the city illustrate the <a href="/wiki/Serbo-Byzantine_architecture" title="Serbo-Byzantine architecture">Vardar architectural school</a> which flourished around 1300. Among these churches are the ones around <a href="/wiki/Matka_Canyon" title="Matka Canyon">Matka Canyon</a> (St Nicholas, St Andrew and Matka churches). The <a href="/wiki/Church_of_St._Panteleimon_(Gorno_Nerezi)" title="Church of St. Panteleimon (Gorno Nerezi)">church of St. Panteleimon</a> in <a href="/wiki/Gorno_Nerezi" title="Gorno Nerezi">Gorno Nerezi</a> dates from the 12th century. Its expressive frescoes anticipate the <a href="/wiki/Italian_primitives" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian primitives">Italian primitives</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[190]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Isak_Bey_Turbe_Aladja_Mosque_Skopje.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Isak_Bey_Turbe_Aladja_Mosque_Skopje.JPG/220px-Isak_Bey_Turbe_Aladja_Mosque_Skopje.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Isak_Bey_Turbe_Aladja_Mosque_Skopje.JPG/330px-Isak_Bey_Turbe_Aladja_Mosque_Skopje.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Isak_Bey_Turbe_Aladja_Mosque_Skopje.JPG/440px-Isak_Bey_Turbe_Aladja_Mosque_Skopje.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Isak_Bey_Turbe_Aladja_Mosque_Skopje.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aladža Mosque and its türbe.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Examples of <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_architecture" title="Ottoman architecture">Ottoman Turkish architecture</a> are located in the <a href="/wiki/Old_Bazaar,_Skopje" title="Old Bazaar, Skopje">Old Bazaar</a>. <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">Mosques</a> in Skopje are usually simple in design, with a square base and a single <a href="/wiki/Dome" title="Dome">dome</a> and <a href="/wiki/Minaret" title="Minaret">minaret</a>. There entrance is usually emphasised by a portico, as on <a href="/wiki/Mustafa_Pasha_Mosque" title="Mustafa Pasha Mosque">Mustafa Pasha Mosque</a>, dating from the 15th century. Some mosques show some originality in their appearance: <a href="/wiki/Sultan_Murad_Mosque" title="Sultan Murad Mosque">Sultan Murad</a> and Yahya Pasha mosques have lost their dome and have a pyramidal roof, while Isa Bey mosque has a rectangular base, two domes and two side wings. The Aladža Mosque was originally covered with blue faience, but it disappeared in the 1689 Great Fire. However, some tiles are still visible on the adjoining <a href="/wiki/T%C3%BCrbe" title="Türbe">türbe</a>. Other Turkish public monuments include the 16th-century clock tower, a <a href="/wiki/Bedesten" title="Bedesten">bedesten</a>, three <a href="/wiki/Caravanserai" title="Caravanserai">caravanserais</a>, two <a href="/wiki/Turkish_baths" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish baths">Turkish baths</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Stone_Bridge_(Skopje)" title="Stone Bridge (Skopje)">Stone Bridge</a>, first mentioned in 1469.<sup id="cite_ref-ottoman_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ottoman-83">[80]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-oldskopje_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oldskopje-194">[191]</a></sup></p>
<p>The oldest churches in the city centre, the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Ascension_of_Jesus,_Skopje" title="Church of the Ascension of Jesus, Skopje">Ascension</a> and St Dimitri churches, were built in the 18th century, after the 1689 Great Fire. They were both renovated in the 19th century. The Church of the Ascension is particularly small it is half-buried in order not to overlook neighbouring mosques.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[192]</a></sup> In the 19th century, several new churches were built, including the Church of the Nativity of the Virgin Mary, which is a large three-nave building designed by <a href="/wiki/Andrey_Damyanov" title="Andrey Damyanov">Andrey Damyanov</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[193]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Po%C5%A1ta_vo_Skopje,_Macedonia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Po%C5%A1ta_vo_Skopje%2C_Macedonia.jpg/220px-Po%C5%A1ta_vo_Skopje%2C_Macedonia.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Po%C5%A1ta_vo_Skopje%2C_Macedonia.jpg/330px-Po%C5%A1ta_vo_Skopje%2C_Macedonia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Po%C5%A1ta_vo_Skopje%2C_Macedonia.jpg/440px-Po%C5%A1ta_vo_Skopje%2C_Macedonia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Po%C5%A1ta_vo_Skopje,_Macedonia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Main post office and the Communication Centre.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After 1912, when Skopje was annexed by Serbia, the city was drastically westernised. Wealthy Serbs built mansions and town houses such as the 1926 <a href="/wiki/Risti%E1%B8%B1_Palace" title="Ristiḱ Palace">Ristiḱ Palace</a>. Architecture of that time is very similar to the one of <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central Europe</a>, but some buildings are more creative, such as the <a href="/wiki/Moorish_Revival_architecture" title="Moorish Revival architecture">Neo-Moorish</a> Arab House and the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Revival_architecture" title="Byzantine Revival architecture">Neo-Byzantine</a> train station, both built in 1938.<sup id="cite_ref-colophon_100-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-colophon-100">[97]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Modernist_architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Modernist architecture">Modernism</a> appeared as early as 1933 with the former Ethnographic Museum (today the City Gallery), designed by <a href="/wiki/Milan_Zlokovi%C4%87" title="Milan Zloković">Milan Zloković</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-colophon_100-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-colophon-100">[97]</a></sup> However, modernist architecture only fully developed in Skopje after the 1963 earthquake. The reconstruction of city centre was partially planned by Japanese <a href="/wiki/Kenzo_Tange" class="mw-redirect" title="Kenzo Tange">Kenzo Tange</a> who designed the new train station.<sup id="cite_ref-colophon_100-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-colophon-100">[97]</a></sup> Macedonian architects also took part to the reconstruction: <a href="/wiki/Georgi_Konstantinovski" title="Georgi Konstantinovski">Georgi Konstantinovski</a> designed the City Archives building in 1968 and the Hall of residence Goce Delčev in 1975, while <a href="/wiki/Janko_Konstantinov" title="Janko Konstantinov">Janko Konstantinov</a> designed the Telecommunication Centre and the main post office (1974–1989). <a href="/wiki/Slavko_Brezovski" class="mw-redirect" title="Slavko Brezovski">Slavko Brezovski</a> designed the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_St._Clement_of_Ohrid" title="Church of St. Clement of Ohrid">Church of St. Clement of Ohrid</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[194]</a></sup> These two buildings are noted for their originality although they are directly inspired by <a href="/wiki/Brutalist_architecture" title="Brutalist architecture">brutalism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-colophon_100-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-colophon-100">[97]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Arch%C3%A4ologisches_Museum_von_Mazedonien_(Skopje).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Arch%C3%A4ologisches_Museum_von_Mazedonien_%28Skopje%29.jpg/220px-Arch%C3%A4ologisches_Museum_von_Mazedonien_%28Skopje%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Arch%C3%A4ologisches_Museum_von_Mazedonien_%28Skopje%29.jpg/330px-Arch%C3%A4ologisches_Museum_von_Mazedonien_%28Skopje%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Arch%C3%A4ologisches_Museum_von_Mazedonien_%28Skopje%29.jpg/440px-Arch%C3%A4ologisches_Museum_von_Mazedonien_%28Skopje%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3259" data-file-height="2446" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Arch%C3%A4ologisches_Museum_von_Mazedonien_(Skopje).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Archeological Museum of Macedonia.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The reconstruction turned Skopje into a proper modernist city, with large blocks of flats, austere concrete buildings and scattered green spaces. The city centre was considered as a grey and unattractive place when local authorities unveiled the "<a href="/wiki/Skopje_2014" title="Skopje 2014">Skopje 2014</a>" project in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[195]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[196]</a></sup> It made plans to erect a large number of statues, fountains, bridges, and museums at a cost of about €500&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[197]</a></sup></p>
<p>The project has generated controversy: critics have described the new landmark buildings as signs of reactionary <a href="/wiki/Historicism_(art)" title="Historicism (art)">historicist</a> aesthetics.<sup id="cite_ref-Skopje2014_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skopje2014-201">[198]</a></sup> Also, the government has been criticised for its cost and for the original lack of representation of national minorities in the coverage of its set of statues and memorials.<sup id="cite_ref-Skopje2014_201-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skopje2014-201">[198]</a></sup> However, representations of minorities have since been included among the monuments. The scheme is accused of turning Skopje to a <a href="/wiki/Theme_park" class="mw-redirect" title="Theme park">theme park</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[199]</a></sup> which is viewed as nationalistic kitsch,<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[200]</a></sup> and has made Skopje an example to see how national identities are constructed and how this construction is mirrored in the urban space.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHeroldLangerLechler2010.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3Dsgfc1TosZGYC.26pg.3DPA43.26dq.3Dantiquization.26hl.3Den.26sa.3DX.26ei.3DaW0VT52IIJHXsgbZ6vgX.26redir_esc.3Dy.23v.3Donepage.26q.3Dantiquization.26f.3Dfalse_43.5D_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeroldLangerLechler2010.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3Dsgfc1TosZGYC.26pg.3DPA43.26dq.3Dantiquization.26hl.3Den.26sa.3DX.26ei.3DaW0VT52IIJHXsgbZ6vgX.26redir_esc.3Dy.23v.3Donepage.26q.3Dantiquization.26f.3Dfalse_43.5D-204">[201]</a></sup></p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 164.66666666667px">
<div style="width: 164.66666666667px">

</div>
</div>
</li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 138px">
<div style="width: 138px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 136px;">
<div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mustafa_Pa%C5%9Fa_Mosque,_Skopje_-_interior.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Mustafa_Pa%C5%9Fa_Mosque%2C_Skopje_-_interior.jpg/204px-Mustafa_Pa%C5%9Fa_Mosque%2C_Skopje_-_interior.jpg" width="136" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Mustafa_Pa%C5%9Fa_Mosque%2C_Skopje_-_interior.jpg/306px-Mustafa_Pa%C5%9Fa_Mosque%2C_Skopje_-_interior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Mustafa_Pa%C5%9Fa_Mosque%2C_Skopje_-_interior.jpg/408px-Mustafa_Pa%C5%9Fa_Mosque%2C_Skopje_-_interior.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2178" data-file-height="1920" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="gallerytext">

</div>
</div>
</li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals">Festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Skopje_Jazz_Festival" title="Skopje Jazz Festival">Skopje Jazz Festival</a> has been held annually in October since 1981. It is part of the European Jazz Network and the European Forum of World Wide Festivals. The artists' profiles include fusion, <a href="/wiki/Acid_jazz" title="Acid jazz">acid jazz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latin_jazz" title="Latin jazz">Latin jazz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Smooth_jazz" title="Smooth jazz">smooth jazz</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Avant-garde_jazz" title="Avant-garde jazz">avant-garde jazz</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ray_Charles" title="Ray Charles">Ray Charles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tito_Puente" title="Tito Puente">Tito Puente</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gotan_Project" title="Gotan Project">Gotan Project</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Di_Meola" title="Al Di Meola">Al Di Meola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Youssou_N%27Dour" title="Youssou N'Dour">Youssou N'Dour</a>, among others, have performed at the festival. Another music festival in Skopje is the Blues and Soul Festival. It is a relatively new event in the Macedonian cultural scene that occurs every summer in early July.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[202]</a></sup> Past guests include <a href="/wiki/Larry_Coryell" title="Larry Coryell">Larry Coryell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mick_Taylor" title="Mick Taylor">Mick Taylor</a> &amp; the All-Stars Blues Band, <a href="/wiki/Candy_Dulfer" title="Candy Dulfer">Candy Dulfer</a> &amp; Funky Stuff, <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Bosco" title="João Bosco">João Bosco</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Temptations" title="The Temptations">The Temptations</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tolo_Marton&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tolo Marton (page does not exist)">Tolo Marton</a> Trio, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Blues_Wire&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Blues Wire (page does not exist)">Blues Wire</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Phil_Guy" title="Phil Guy">Phil Guy</a>.</p>
<p>The Skopje Cultural Summer Festival is a renowned cultural event that takes place in Skopje each year during the summer. The festival is a member of the <a href="/wiki/International_Festivals_and_Events_Association" title="International Festivals and Events Association">International Festivals and Events Association</a> (IFEA) and it includes musical concerts, operas, ballets, plays, art and photograph exhibitions, movies, and multimedia projects that gather 2,000 participants from around the world each year including the <a href="/wiki/St_Petersburg" class="mw-redirect" title="St Petersburg">St Petersburg</a> Theatre, the Chamber Orchestra of the <a href="/wiki/Bolshoi_Theatre" title="Bolshoi Theatre">Bolshoi Theatre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Irina_Arkhipova" title="Irina Arkhipova">Irina Arkhipova</a>, <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Tretiakov" title="Viktor Tretiakov">Viktor Tretiakov</a>, The Theatre of Shadows, <a href="/wiki/Michel_Dalberto" title="Michel Dalberto">Michel Dalberto</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dave_Burgess_(musician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dave Burgess (musician)">David Burgess</a>.</p>
<p>May Opera Evenings is a festival that has occurred annually in Skopje since 1972 and is dedicated to promoting opera among the general public. Over the years, it has evolved into a stage on which artists from some 50 countries have performed. There is one other major international theater festival that takes place each year at the end of month September, the Young Open Theater Festival (MOT), which was organized for the first time in May 1976 by the Youth Cultural Center – Skopje.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[203]</a></sup> More than 700 theatrical performances have been presented at this festival so far, most of them being alternative, <a href="/wiki/Experimental_theatre" title="Experimental theatre">experimental theatre</a> groups engaging young writers and actors. The MOT International theater festival is also a member of the International Network for Contemporary Performing Arts or IETM.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[204]</a></sup> Within the framework of the MOT Festival, the Macedonian National Center of the International Theater Institute (ITI) was established, and at the 25th ITI World Congress in Munich in 1993, it became a regular member of this theater association. The festival has an international character, always representing theaters from all over the world that present and enhance exchange and circulation of young-fresh-experimental-avant guard theatrical energy and experience between its participants on one side and the audience on the other.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Skopje_Film_Festival" title="Skopje Film Festival">Skopje Film Festival</a> is an annual event held in the city every March. Over 50 films are shown at this five-day festival, mostly from Macedonia and Europe, but also including some non-commercial film productions from all over the world.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nightlife">Nightlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Nightlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Skopije_at_night.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Skopije_at_night.jpg/220px-Skopije_at_night.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Skopije_at_night.jpg/330px-Skopije_at_night.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Skopije_at_night.jpg/440px-Skopije_at_night.jpg 2x" data-file-width="972" data-file-height="648" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Skopije_at_night.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Panorama of Skopje at night.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Skopje has a diverse nightlife. There is a large emphasis on casinos, many of which are associated with hotels, such as that of the Holiday Inn. Other casinos include Helios Metropol, Olympic, Bon Venon, and Sherry.<sup id="cite_ref-Nightlife_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nightlife-208">[205]</a></sup> Among young people the most popular destinations are bars, discos, and nightclubs which can be found in the center and the City Park. Among the most popular nightclubs are Midnight, Hard Rock, Maracana, B2, Havana and Colosseum where world-famous disc jockeys and idiosyncratic local performances are frequent. In 2010, the Colosseum club was named fifth on a list of the best clubs in Southeastern Europe. <a href="/wiki/Armin_van_Buuren" title="Armin van Buuren">Armin van Buuren</a>, <a href="/wiki/Above_and_Beyond_(band)" class="mw-redirect" title="Above and Beyond (band)">Above and Beyond</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shapeshifters_(music_act)" class="mw-redirect" title="Shapeshifters (music act)">The Shapeshifters</a> are just some of the many musicians that have visited the club.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[206]</a></sup> Nighttime concerts in local, regional and global music are often held at the <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_Arena" title="Philip II Arena">Philip II National Arena</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boris_Trajkovski_Sports_Center" title="Boris Trajkovski Sports Center">Boris Trajkovski Sports Center</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Nightlife_208-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nightlife-208">[205]</a></sup> For middle-aged people, places for having fun are also the <i><a href="/wiki/Kafana" title="Kafana">kafeanas</a></i> where traditional <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_the_Republic_of_Macedonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuisine of the Republic of Macedonia">Macedonian food</a> is served and traditional <a href="/wiki/Music_of_the_Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Music of the Republic of Macedonia">Macedonian Music</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Starogradska_muzika" title="Starogradska muzika">Starogradska muzika</a></i>) is played, but <a href="/wiki/Balkan_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Balkan music">music from all the Balkans</a>, particularly <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Serbia" title="Music of Serbia">Serbian folk music</a> is also popular. Apart from the traditional Macedonian restaurants, there are restaurants featuring international cuisines.<sup id="cite_ref-Nightlife_208-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nightlife-208">[205]</a></sup> Some of the most popular cafés in Skopje are Café Ei8ht, Café Trend, Drama Café, Lex Café and Blue Café. The <a href="/wiki/Old_Bazaar,_Skopje" title="Old Bazaar, Skopje">Old Bazaar</a> was a popular nightlife destination in the past. The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_Republic_of_Macedonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Government of the Republic of Macedonia">national government</a> has created a project to revive nightlife in the Old Bazaar. The closing time in shops, cafés and restaurants was extended due to the high attendances recorded. In the bazaar's restaurants, along with the traditional Macedonian wine and food, dishes of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_cuisine" title="Ottoman cuisine">Ottoman cuisine</a> are also served.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[207]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="People_from_Skopje">People from Skopje</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skopje&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: People from Skopje">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Skopje" title="List of people from Skopje">List of people from Skopje</a></div>
<p>Notable people from Skopje include:</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2;">
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Justinian_I" title="Justinian I">Justinian I</a>, <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Emperor" class="mw-redirect" title="Byzantine Emperor">Byzantine Emperor</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Konstantin_Tih" title="Konstantin Tih">Konstantin Tih</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Tsar" class="mw-redirect" title="Bulgarian Tsar">Bulgarian Tsar</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mother_Teresa" title="Mother Teresa">Mother Teresa</a>, Roman Catholic humanitarian (honorary citizen of Skopje 27 June 1980)<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[208]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ljubi%C5%A1a_Samard%C5%BEi%C4%87" title="Ljubiša Samardžić">Ljubiša Samardžić</a>, actor and film director</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Blagoje_Vidini%C4%87" title="Blagoje Vidinić">Blagoje Vidinić</a>, footballer and Olympic champion</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Blagoja_Georgievski" title="Blagoja Georgievski">Blagoja Georgievski</a>, basketball player and Olympic silver medalist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Stojna_Vangelovska" title="Stojna Vangelovska">Stojna Vangelovska</a>, basketball player and Olympic silver medalist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pero_Anti%C4%87" title="Pero Antić">Pero Antić</a>, basketball and NBA player</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Esma_Red%C5%BEepova" title="Esma Redžepova">Esma Redžepova</a>, vocalist, songwriter, and humanitarian</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Blagoje_Vidini%C4%87" title="Blagoje Vidinić">Blagoje Vidinić</a>, footballer and Olympic bronze medalist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Darko_Pan%C4%8Dev" title="Darko Pančev">Darko Pančev</a>, former footballer, European Cup champion</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Simon_Trp%C4%8Deski" title="Simon Trpčeski">Simon Trpčeski</a>, pianist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Srgjan_Kerim" title="Srgjan Kerim">Srgjan Kerim</a>, former UN General Assembly president</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Yahya_Kemal_Beyatl%C4%B1" title="Yahya Kemal Beyatlı">Yahya Kemal Beyatlı</a>, poet and diplomat</li>
</ul>
</div>
